$$\sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i = \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}) = \mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}) = \hat{\mathbf{v}} \,.$$

The 1st equality is by definition of  $\hat{\mathbf{v}}_i$ ; the 2nd equality holds because (i) the map  $g_{\vec{\mathbf{r}}}(f) := f(\vec{\mathbf{r}})$  satisfies that  $g_{\vec{\mathbf{r}}}(a \cdot f_1 + b \cdot f_2) = a \cdot g_{\vec{\mathbf{r}}}(f_1) + b \cdot g_{\vec{\mathbf{r}}}(f_2)$  for any multilinear polynomials  $f_1, f_2$  and  $a, b \in \mathbb{Z}_q$ ; and (ii)  $\hat{\mathbf{f}} = \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \hat{\mathbf{f}}_i$  given that

$$\mathsf{NTT}(\widehat{\mathbf{f}}) = \mathsf{Coef}\left(\widehat{\mathbf{f}}^i\right) = \mathsf{Coef}\left(\sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \widehat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right) = \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \mathsf{Coef}\left(\widehat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right) = \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \mathsf{NTT}(\widehat{\mathbf{f}}_i) = \mathsf{NTT}\left(\sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \widehat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right) \,.$$

The last equality holds because  $(pp, x; w) \in \mathcal{R}^B_{hom}$  by assumption. Thus, V accepts in the honest execution.

Next, we show that  $(\mathsf{pp}, [(\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, y_i); \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=0}^{k-1})$  is in  $\mathcal{R}_2 := (\mathcal{R}^b_{\mathsf{hom}})^k$ . For every  $i \in [0, k)$ , recall that  $y_i = \mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i)$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{v}}_i = \mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}})$ . Moreover, by definition of  $\mathsf{split}_{b,k}(\vec{\mathbf{f}})$  (Eq. (11)), we have that  $\|\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i\|_{\infty} < b$ . Therefore,  $(\mathsf{pp}, (\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, y_i); \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i) \in \mathcal{R}^b_{\mathsf{hom}}$  and completeness holds.

## <span id="page-23-0"></span>**Lemma 3.5.** $\Pi_{\text{dec}}^*$ satisfies knowledge soundness.

*Proof.* Let  $(\mathbf{x} := (\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}, y); \mathsf{state}) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(\mathsf{pp})$  denote adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ 's chosen input instance for  $\mathcal{R}_1 := \mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{hom}}$ , where  $\mathsf{pp} := (\mathcal{R}_q, m, B < q/2, \mathcal{L}) \leftarrow \mathsf{Setup}(1^{\lambda})$  is the public parameter. The extractor Ext proceeds as follows:

- 1. Simulate the protocol  $\langle P^*(pp, x, state), V(pp, x) \rangle$  where  $P^*$  is the malicious prover.
- 2. Output  $\perp$  if V rejects. Otherwise let  $(\mathbf{z}_o, \mathbf{w}_o) := [(\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, y_i); \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=0}^{k-1}$  be the protocol output. (Note that  $\vec{\mathbf{r}}$  is the same with that in the input instance  $\mathbf{z}$  to pass the verification check.) The extractor outputs witness

$$\mathbf{w} := \vec{\mathbf{f}} := \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i \,. \tag{12}$$

Next, we show that if V accepts and the output satisfies that  $(\mathbf{pp}, \mathbf{z}_o, \mathbf{w}_o)$  is in  $\mathcal{R}_2 := (\mathcal{R}^b_{\mathsf{hom}})^k$ , then the extracted witness  $\vec{\mathbf{f}}$  satisfies that  $(\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}, y; \vec{\mathbf{f}}) \in \mathcal{R}_1 := \mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{hom}}$ . Since V accepts, we have that  $y = \sum_{i=0}^{2k-1} b^i \cdot y_i$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{v}} = \sum_{i=0}^{2k-1} b^i \cdot \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i$ . Recall that  $y_i = \mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i)$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{v}}_i = \mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}})$  for all  $i \in [0, k)$  by assumption, thus by Lemma 3.2, we have that  $y = \mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{f}})$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{v}} = \mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}})$ . Moreover, note that  $\|\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i\|_{\infty} < b$  for all  $i \in [0, k)$  because  $(\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, y_i; \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i)$  is in  $\mathcal{R}^b_{\mathsf{hom}}$  by assumption. Since  $b^k = B < q/2$  and  $\vec{\mathbf{f}} = \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i$ , we have

$$\|\vec{\mathbf{f}}\|_{\infty} = \|\sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i\|_{\infty} \le \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \|\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i\|_{\infty} \le \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot (b-1) < b^k = B.$$

In summary,  $y = \mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{f}})$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{v}} = \mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}})$  and  $\|\vec{\mathbf{f}}\|_{\infty} < B$  and thus  $(\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}, y; \vec{\mathbf{f}}) \in \mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{hom}}$ .

# <span id="page-24-0"></span>**3.2.3** Folding: The reduction from $(\mathcal{R}_{\text{eval}}^b)^{2k}$ to $\mathcal{R}_{\text{eval}}^B$

We now describe the core protocol  $\Pi_{\text{fold}}$  that folds 2k instance-witness pairs of  $\mathcal{R}^b_{\text{eval}}$  from (9) into a single instance-witness pair in  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\text{eval}}$ . More generally, the protocol is a reduction of knowledge from  $(\mathcal{R}^b_{\text{hom}})^{2k}$  from (10) to  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\text{hom}}$  with a further restriction that the public parameter, the sampled homomorphism  $\mathcal{L}$ , is **relaxed binding** as in Section 2.3. This relaxed binding property, defined for bound 2B and the challenge space  $\mathcal{C}_{\text{small}}$ , ensures the hardness of finding two distinct weak openings for a commitment cm. Recall that a 2B-weak opening ( $\rho \in \mathcal{C}_{\text{small}} - \mathcal{C}_{\text{small}}, \vec{\mathbf{x}}$ ) of cm satisfies that  $\rho \cdot \text{cm} = \mathbf{A}\vec{\mathbf{x}} \mod q$  with the norm constraint  $\|\vec{\mathbf{x}}\|_{\infty} < 2B$ . Thus,  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\text{eval}}$  from (9) is a special case of  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\text{hom}}$  where the sampled homomorphism  $\mathcal{L}$  is given by  $\mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{f}}) := \mathbf{A}\vec{\mathbf{f}}$ , and the 2B-relaxed binding property follows from the hardness of  $\text{MSIS}^{\infty,q}_{\kappa,m,8TB}$  where  $T = \|\mathcal{C}_{\text{small}}\|_{\text{op}}$  is the expansion factor of  $\mathcal{C}_{\text{small}}$ .

Our protocol folds the 2k witness vectors (with norm less than b) into a witness vector of norm less than B (where b < B < q/2), using small random scalars  $[\rho_i]_{i=1}^{2k}$  sampled from a strong sampling set  $\mathcal{C}_{small} \subseteq \mathcal{R}_q$ . Additionally and crucially,  $\Pi_{\text{fold}}$  runs a sum-check protocol to enable extractions of the 2k witness vectors with small norms. The sum-check is for a polynomial  $g(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) := \sum_{i=1}^{2k} (\alpha_i g_{1,i}(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) + \mu_i g_{2,i}(\vec{\mathbf{x}}))$  with random scalars  $[\alpha_i, \mu_i]_{i=1}^{2k}$ . Informally, we can understand it as a batch of 4k separate sum-checks for polynomials  $[g_{1,i}, g_{2,i}]_{i=1}^{2k}$ , respectively. The sum-check for  $g_{1,i}$  (defined in Eq. (15)) is used to verify that the evaluation statement  $\mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i) = \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i$  holds for all  $i \in [2k]$ . For every  $i \in [2k]$ , the sum-check for  $g_{2,i}$  (defined in Eq. (16)) is used to verify that

$$\prod_{j=-(b-1)}^{b-1} \left( \mathsf{mle} \left[ \hat{\mathbf{f}}_i \right] (\vec{\mathbf{x}}) - j \right) = 0 \quad \text{for all } \vec{\mathbf{x}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}$$

This is the same as the Hadamard product check (the norm bound check)

$$\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i \circ \left[ \bigcirc_{j=1}^{b-1} (\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i - \hat{j}) \circ (\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i + \hat{j}) \right] = \hat{0},$$

in the relation  $\mathcal{R}^b_{\mathsf{cm}}$  from (8).

We describe the protocol  $\Pi_{\text{fold}}$  in Figure 3. We now see why the relation  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\text{cm}}$  from (8) had to be expanded to the related  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\text{eval}}$  from (9). Protocol  $\Pi_{\text{fold}}$  reduces the claimed properties about the 2k input instances to verifying that  $\mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_o\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o) = \hat{\mathbf{v}}_o$ , where  $(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_o)$  is part of the output folded instance. Adding this evaluation check to the relation  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\text{eval}}$  forces the prover to output a folded statement that satisfies this equality. The verifier cannot check this relation itself as part of  $\Pi_{\text{fold}}$  because it does not have access to  $\vec{\mathbf{f}}_o$ .

The following lemma shows that the protocol  $\Pi_{\text{fold}}$  in Figure 3 is a reduction of knowledge from  $(\mathcal{R}_{\text{hom}}^b)^{2k}$  to  $\mathcal{R}_{\text{hom}}^B$  assuming that  $\mathcal{L}$  is a relaxed binding.

**Parameters:** Strong sampling sets  $\mathcal{C}, \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}} \subseteq \mathcal{R}_q$  where  $\mathcal{C}$  is defined as in Eq. (31) and  $\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}$  has expansion factor  $\|\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}\|_{\mathsf{op}} \leq c \in \mathbb{N}$  as in (6).

Input:  $[\mathbf{z}_i := (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, y_i) \in \mathcal{R}_q^{\log m} \times \mathcal{R}_q \times \mathcal{Y}]_{i=1}^{2k}$  and  $[\mathbf{w}_i := \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i \in \mathcal{R}_q^m]_{i=1}^{2k}$ 

Output:  $x_o := (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_o, y_o), w_o := \vec{\mathbf{f}}_o$ 

The protocol  $\langle \mathsf{P}(\mathsf{pp}, \mathsf{x}; \mathsf{w}), \mathsf{V}(\mathsf{pp}, \mathsf{x}) \rangle$  where  $\mathsf{x} = [\mathsf{x}_i]_{i=1}^{2k}$  and  $\mathsf{w} = [\mathsf{w}_i]_{i=1}^{2k}$ : 1.  $\mathsf{V} \to \mathsf{P} : \mathsf{V}$  sends  $\mathsf{P}$  challenges  $[\alpha_i, \mu_i]_{i=1}^{2k} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} (\mathcal{C} \times \mathcal{C})^{2k}$  and  $\vec{\beta} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{C}^{\log m}$ .

- 2.  $V \leftrightarrow P : P$  and V run a sum-check protocol for the claim

<span id="page-25-5"></span><span id="page-25-3"></span><span id="page-25-2"></span><span id="page-25-1"></span>
$$\sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}} g(\vec{\mathbf{b}}) = \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \alpha_i \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, \qquad (13)$$

where the polynomial  $g(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) \in \mathcal{R}_q^{\leq 2b}[X_1, \dots, X_{\log m}]$  is defined as

$$g(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) := g_{\text{eval}}(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) + g_{\text{norm}}(\vec{\mathbf{x}}), \tag{14}$$

$$g_{\text{eval}}(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) := \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \alpha_i \cdot g_{1,i}(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) \quad \text{where} \quad g_{1,i}(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) := eq(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i, \vec{\mathbf{x}}) \cdot \text{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right](\vec{\mathbf{x}}), \tag{15}$$

$$g_{\mathsf{norm}}(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) := \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \mu_i \cdot g_{2,i}(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) \quad \text{where} \quad g_{2,i}(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) := eq(\vec{\beta}, \vec{\mathbf{x}}) \cdot \prod_{j=-(b-1)}^{b-1} \left( \mathsf{mle} \left[ \hat{\mathbf{f}}_i \right] (\vec{\mathbf{x}}) - j \right) \quad (16)$$

The sumcheck protocol reduces checking (13) to checking the evaluation claim  $g(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o) \stackrel{?}{=} s$ , where  $s \in \mathcal{R}_q$  and  $\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{C}^{\log m}$  is a sum-check challenge sampled by  $\mathsf{V}$ .

- 3.  $P \to V : P \text{ sends } V \text{ values } \left[\theta_i := \mathsf{mle} \left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right] (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o)\right]_{i=1}^{2k}$ .
- <span id="page-25-4"></span>4. V computes  $[\mathbf{e}_i := eq(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i, \vec{\mathbf{r}}_o)]_{i=1}^{2k}$  and  $\mathbf{e}^* := eq(\vec{\beta}, \vec{\mathbf{r}}_o)$  and checks that

$$s \stackrel{?}{=} \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \left[ \alpha_i \mathbf{e}_i \theta_i + \mu_i \mathbf{e}^* \cdot \prod_{j=1-b}^{b-1} (\theta_i - j) \right].$$

- 5.  $V \to P : V \text{ sends } P \text{ random challenge } [\rho_i]_{i=1}^{2k} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}^{2k}$
- 6. V outputs  $\mathbf{z}_o := (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_o, y_o)$  where

$$\mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{v}}_o) = \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \mathsf{RotSum}(\rho_i, \mathsf{NTT}(\theta_i)) \,, \qquad y_o := \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \rho_i y_i \,.$$

7. P further outputs  $w_o := \vec{\mathbf{f}}_o = \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \rho_i \cdot \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i$ .

<span id="page-25-0"></span>Figure 3: The protocol  $\Pi_{\text{fold}}$  beat reduces  $(\mathcal{R}_{\text{hom}}^b)^{2k}$  to  $\mathcal{R}_{\text{hom}}^B$ 

<sup>&</sup>lt;sup>a</sup>If  $\mathcal{R}_q \cong \mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}^{d/\tau}$  for some  $\tau > 1$ , the value  $\hat{\mathbf{v}}_o$  is replaced with  $\hat{V}_o \in \mathcal{R}_q^{\tau}$  and verifier check is modified as in Eq. (32).

<span id="page-26-0"></span>**Theorem 3.2.** Let  $\mathcal{R}_q \cong \mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}^{d/\tau}$  for some  $\tau \in \mathbb{N}$  where  $\tau \mid d$  and  $1/q^{\tau}$  is in  $\mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ . Let  $\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}} \subseteq \mathcal{R}_q$  be a strong sampling set for which  $1/|\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}||$  is in  $\mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ , and the expansion factor  $\|\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}\|_{\mathsf{op}} \leq c$  (Definition 6) for some  $c \in \mathbb{N}$ . Let  $\mathcal{C}$  be the strong sampling set as in Eq. (31). Let  $\mathsf{pp} := (m, B < q/2, \mathcal{L})$  be the public parameters where the sampled  $\mathcal{R}_q$ -module homomorphism  $\mathcal{L} : \mathcal{R}_q^m \to \mathcal{Y}$  is a 2B-relaxed binding (Section 2.3) for challenge space  $\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}$ . For any b, k where 2kc(b-1) < B, the protocol  $\Pi_{\mathsf{fold}}$  is a reduction of knowledge from  $(\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{hom}}^b)^{2k}$  to  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{hom}}^B$ .

**Remark 3.2.**  $\Pi_{\text{fold}}$  (*Figure 3*) uses two different sampling sets C,  $C_{\text{small}}$  where C is for sumcheck and  $C_{\text{small}}$  is for folding. We set C as in Eq. (31) for two reasons:

- 1. Sumcheck efficiency: By Eq. (31), for every  $\mathbf{a}_i \in \mathcal{C}$ ,  $\mathsf{NTT}(\mathbf{a}_i) = (i, \dots, i)$  where  $i \in \mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}$  is the embedding of  $\mathbf{a}_i$  in  $\mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}$ . So  $\mathcal{C}$  lets us treat the sumcheck over  $\mathcal{R}_q$  as  $d/\tau$  parallel sumchecks over  $\mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}$  that share the same sumcheck challenge vector over  $\mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}^{\log m}$ , and no NTT transformation is needed when running the sumcheck. Note that the removal of the NTT transform also improves the circuit size of the sumcheck verifier.
- 2. Completeness: As discussed in Remark 3.1 and Section 3.3, Lemma 3.2 still holds when C is set as in Eq. (31). This is essential for the folding protocol to support small modulus q.

For the special case  $\mathcal{R}_q \cong \mathbb{Z}_q^d$ , the proof follows from Lemma 3.6 and Theorem 3.3 below. As discussed in Section 3.3, with a minor modification to the protocol, the proof naturally extends to the case where  $\mathcal{R}_q \cong \mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}^{d/\tau}$ .

<span id="page-26-1"></span>**Lemma 3.6.**  $\Pi_{\mathsf{fold}}$  satisfies public reducibility and completeness.

*Proof.* Public reducibility: Given input instances  $[\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, y_i]_{i=1}^{2k}$  and the transcript that includes the challenge  $\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o$ , evaluations  $[\theta_i]_{i=1}^{2k}$  and folding challenges  $[\rho_i]_{i=1}^{2k}$ . The algorithm outputs  $\mathbf{z}_o := (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_o, y_o := \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \rho_i \cdot y_i)$  where  $\mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{v}}_o) = \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \mathsf{RotSum}(\rho_i, \mathsf{NTT}(\theta_i))$  if the verification passes. Otherwise, it outputs  $\bot$ .

<u>Completeness:</u> Let  $(\mathbf{x}, \mathbf{w}) := [\mathbf{x}_i = (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, y_i), \mathbf{w}_i = \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{2k} \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(\mathsf{pp})$  denote adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ 's chosen input for  $\mathcal{R}_1 := (\mathcal{R}^b_{\mathsf{hom}})^{2k}$ , where  $\mathsf{pp} := (\mathcal{R}_q, m, B < q/2, \mathcal{L}) \leftarrow \mathsf{Setup}(1^{\lambda})$  is the public parameter. WLOG we assume that  $(\mathsf{pp}, \mathbf{x}_i, \mathbf{w}_i) \in \mathcal{R}^b_{\mathsf{hom}}$  for all  $i \in [2k]$ . The protocol  $\langle \mathsf{P}(\mathsf{pp}, \mathbf{x}, \mathbf{w}), \mathsf{V}(\mathsf{pp}, \mathbf{x}) \rangle$  proceeds as follows:

- 1. P and V honestly run the sum-check and P sends the correct evaluations  $[\theta_i := \text{mle } [\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i] (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o)]_{i=1}^{2k}$ .
- 2. V outputs  $\perp$  and halts if the check at Step 4 fails.

3. Otherwise, let  $[\rho_i]_{i=1}^{2k}$  be verifier's last folding challenges. P outputs  $w_o := \vec{\mathbf{f}}_o := \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \rho_i \cdot \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i$  and V outputs  $z_o := (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_o, y_o)$  where  $\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o$  is V's sum-check challenges and  $(\hat{\mathbf{v}}_o, y_o)$  are defined such that

$$\mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{v}}_o) = \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \mathsf{RotSum}(\rho_i, \mathsf{NTT}(\theta_i))\,, \qquad y_o := \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \rho_i \cdot y_i\,.$$

We first show that V accepts, i.e., the check at Step 4 passes. This follows by definition of the polynomial g (Eq. (14)) and by definition of P's sent evaluations.

It remains to argue that the protocol output  $(\mathbf{x}_o, \mathbf{w}_o)$  satisfies that  $(\mathbf{pp}, \mathbf{x}_o, \mathbf{w}_o) \in \mathcal{R}_2 := \mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{hom}}$  (Eq. (10)). First, because  $(\mathbf{pp}, \mathbf{x}_i, \mathbf{w}_i) \in \mathcal{R}^b_{\mathsf{hom}}$  for all  $i \in [2k]$ , by Lemma 3.2, it holds that  $\mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_o) = y_o$  and  $\mathsf{mle} \left[ \hat{\mathbf{f}}_o \right] (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o) = \hat{\mathbf{v}}_o$ . Moreover,

$$\|\vec{\mathbf{f}}_o\|_{\infty} = \|\sum_{i=1}^{2k} \rho_i \cdot \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i\|_{\infty} \le \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \|\rho_i \cdot \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i\|_{\infty} \le \sum_{i=1}^{2k} c \cdot \|\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i\|_{\infty} \le \sum_{i=1}^{2k} c \cdot (b-1) < B.$$

The first inequality holds because for any  $a, b \in \mathcal{R}_q^m$  where  $\|a\|_{\infty} + \|b\|_{\infty} < B < q/2$ , we have that  $\|a+b\|_{\infty} \leq \|a\|_{\infty} + \|b\|_{\infty}$ . (The norm  $\|a\|_{\infty}$  for an element a in  $\mathcal{R}_q$  is defined in Remark 2.1.) The 2nd inequality holds as  $\rho_i \in \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}$  and  $\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}$  has expansion factor at most c; the 3rd inequality holds because  $\|\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i\|_{\infty} < b$  for all  $i \in [2k]$  by the assumption that  $(\mathsf{pp}, \mathsf{z}_i; \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i) \in \mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{hom}}^b$ ; the last inequality holds as 2kc(b-1) < B < q/2 by the premise of Theorem 3.2. Thus  $(\mathsf{pp}, \mathsf{z}_o, \mathsf{w}_o)$  is in  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{hom}}^B$  from (10) as required.

<span id="page-27-0"></span>**Theorem 3.3.** Let  $\operatorname{pp} := (\mathcal{R}_q \cong \mathbb{Z}_q^d, m, B < q/2, \mathcal{L}) \leftarrow \operatorname{Setup}(1^{\lambda})$  denote the public parameters and let  $\mathcal{C}$ ,  $\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}} \subseteq \mathcal{R}_q$  be the strong sampling sets defined in Theorem 3.2. Assume that the  $\mathcal{R}_q$ -module homomorphism  $\mathcal{L} : \mathcal{R}_q^m \to \mathcal{Y}$  is 2B-relaxed binding for challenge space  $\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}$  with binding error  $\epsilon_{\mathsf{bind}}$ . There exists an extractor  $\mathsf{Ext}$  such that for any expected polynomial time adversary  $(\mathcal{A}, \mathsf{P}^*)$  with success probability  $\epsilon_{\mathsf{fold}}(\mathcal{A}, \mathsf{P}^*) = 1/\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ , the extractor  $\mathsf{Ext}^{\mathcal{A},\mathsf{P}^*}$  outputs valid witnesses (for input instances) in relation  $(\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{hom}}^b)^{2k}$  with probability at least  $\epsilon_{\mathsf{fold}}(\mathcal{A}, \mathsf{P}^*) - \kappa(\lambda)$  where

$$\kappa(\lambda) := \frac{2k}{|\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}|} + \epsilon_{\mathsf{bind}} + \frac{(2b+1)\log m + 4k}{|\mathcal{C}|}.$$

The expected running time of  $Ext^{A,P^*}$  is at most

$$T_{\mathsf{ext}} := \left(1 + \frac{1}{\epsilon_{\mathsf{fold}}(\mathcal{A}, \mathsf{P}^*) - \frac{2k}{|\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}|}}\right) \cdot (1 + 2k) = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda) \,.$$

*Proof.* As noted by Remark 1 of [AF22], it is without loss of generality to assume that  $(\mathcal{A}, \mathsf{P}^*)$  are deterministic algorithms. For ease of notation, we assume that  $\mathsf{P}^*$  outputs  $\bot$ 

when it fails the verification or its output is not a valid witness for the output instance. We can always transform a prover to satisfy this requirement without affecting the success probability. To simplify the notation in the proof we introduce the following symbols:

- set  $k^* := 2k$
- $\bullet$  the folding challenge space is denoted  $\mathcal{S} := \mathcal{C}^{k^*}_{\mathsf{small}},$
- the remaining challenge space is denoted  $\Psi := \mathcal{C}^{2k^* + 2\log m}$ .

Let us first give some intuition for the extraction strategy. Adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  begins by generating some  $k^*$  instances  $\mathbf{z}_i = (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, \mathbf{y}_i)$  for  $i \in [k^*]$ . The prover  $\mathsf{P}^*$  then takes as input a sequence of random challenges from the verifier. These challenges define a folded statement  $\mathbf{z}_o = (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_o, \mathbf{y}_o)$  and  $\mathsf{P}^*$  outputs a valid witness  $\vec{\mathbf{f}}$  for  $\mathbf{z}_o$  with non-negligible probability. Our extractor needs to use such a  $\mathsf{P}^*$  to output valid witnesses  $\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i$  for  $\mathbf{z}_i = (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, \mathbf{y}_i)$  for all  $i \in [k^*]$ . Let us see how to extract  $\vec{\mathbf{f}}_1$ ; the other witnesses are extracted similarly. The high level approach to extract  $\vec{\mathbf{f}}_1$  is to sample two related folding challenge vectors

$$c_0 := (\rho_1, \rho_2, \dots, \rho_{k^*})$$
 and  $c_1 := (\rho'_1, \rho_2, \dots, \rho_{k^*})$  from  $\mathcal{S} := \mathcal{C}^{k^*}_{\mathsf{small}}$ 

with  $\rho_1 \neq \rho'_1$ . Then run  $\mathsf{P}^*$  once on  $c_0$  and once on  $c_1$ . All other random challenges from the verifier are the same on both runs. We show that with non-negligible probability, the prover  $\mathsf{P}^*$  will return two valid witness  $\vec{\mathbf{w}}_0$  and  $\vec{\mathbf{w}}_1$ . If  $\mathsf{P}^*$  were honest then

$$\vec{\mathbf{w}}_0 = \rho_1 \vec{\mathbf{f}}_1 + \sum_{i=2}^{k^*} \rho_i \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i \quad \text{and} \quad \vec{\mathbf{w}}_1 = \rho_1' \vec{\mathbf{f}}_1 + \sum_{i=2}^{k^*} \rho_i \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i$$

from which it follows that  $(\vec{\mathbf{w}}_0 - \vec{\mathbf{w}}_1) = (\rho_1 - \rho_1')\vec{\mathbf{f}}_1$ . We can now calculate  $\vec{\mathbf{f}}_1$  because  $\rho_1 - \rho_1'$  is invertible in  $\mathcal{R}_q$  (since  $\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}$  is a strong sampling set). However,  $\mathsf{P}^*$  can be malicious. Fortunately, our analysis will show that a slightly enhanced strategy will either extract a valid witness  $\vec{\mathbf{f}}_1$  for  $\mathbf{z}_1$  with non-negligible probability, or break the 2B-relaxed binding property of  $\mathcal{L}$ . In particular, in Claim 3.7 below we show that the sumcheck in protocol  $\Pi_{\mathsf{fold}}$ , combined with the relaxed binding property of  $\mathcal{L}$ , ensures that the extracted witnesses  $\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i$  have norm at most b and that the evaluations of  $\mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right]$  at  $\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i$  are correct.

**The Extractor.** We describe the complete extractor  $\operatorname{Ext}^{\mathcal{A},\mathsf{P}^*}$  in Figure 4. The extractor invokes two sub-procedures. The algorithm  $\mathsf{IG}^{\mathcal{A}}$  samples the input instances. The algorithm  $\mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst},\psi)$ , given randomness  $\psi:=([\alpha_i,\mu_i]_{i=1}^{k^*},\vec{\beta},\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o)$ , tries to recover weak openings to the input instances in inst by rewinding  $\mathsf{P}^*$  multiple times. We emphasize that each run of  $\mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst},\psi)$  and  $\mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst},\psi')$  uses fresh internal randomness for challenges  $(c_0,c_1,\ldots,c_{k^*})$ .

Let  $[\mathbf{z}_i := (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, \mathbf{y}_i)]_{i=1}^{k^*}$  denote the input instances. For any list of length-m ring

```
SubProcedure \mathsf{IG}^{\mathcal{A}}(1^{\lambda}):
                                                           // sample as instance
      1. pp \leftarrow Setup(1^{\lambda})
      2. Return inst := ([x_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}, \text{state}) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(pp)
\frac{\text{SubProcedure SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst}, \psi \in \Psi):}{1. \ c_0 := (\rho_1, \dots, \rho_{k^*}) \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{S}}
                                                                                         // attempt to extract a witness for inst
      2. \vec{\mathbf{w}}_0 \leftarrow \mathsf{P}^*(\mathsf{inst}, c_0, \psi)
      3. If \vec{\mathbf{w}}_0 = \bot return (open, out) := (\bot, \bot)
      4. For i = 1, ..., k^*:
                               // loop until a good folding randomness \rho_i' is found
              (a) \rho_i' \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}} \setminus \{\rho_i\} without replacement
              (b) c_i := (\rho_1, \dots, \rho_{i-1}, \rho'_i, \rho_{i+1}, \dots, \rho_{k^*})
              (c) \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i \leftarrow \mathsf{P}^*(\mathsf{inst}, c_i, \psi)
            Repeat until \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i \neq \perp; return (\perp, \perp) if all \rho'_i have been tried
      5. For i = 1, ..., k^*: set \mathsf{open}_i := (\rho_i - \rho_i', \vec{\mathbf{w}}_0 - \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i) and \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i := (\rho_i - \rho_i')^{-1} (\vec{\mathbf{w}}_0 - \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i)
      6. Return open := [\text{open}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*} and out := [\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}
The extractor \operatorname{Ext}^{\mathcal{A},\mathsf{P}^*}(1^{\lambda}):
      1. inst \leftarrow \mathsf{IG}^{\mathcal{A}}(1^{\lambda})
      2. Do:
                               // loop until a good tuple of challenges \psi is found
              (a) \psi := ([\alpha_i, \mu_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}, \vec{\beta}, \vec{\mathbf{r}}_o) \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \Psi // sample fresh challenges
             \text{(b) } (\mathsf{open}_1,\mathsf{out}_1) \leftarrow \mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst},\psi) \qquad \textit{//} \text{ attempt to extract a witness using } \psi
            Repeat until \mathsf{out}_1 \neq \bot
      3. \psi' := ([\alpha'_i, \mu'_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}, \vec{\beta}', \vec{\mathbf{r}}'_o) \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \Psi
                                                                                 // sample fresh challenges
     4. (\mathsf{open}_2, \mathsf{out}_2) \leftarrow \mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst}, \psi'), abort if \mathsf{out}_2 = \bot or \mathsf{out}_1 \neq \mathsf{out}_2
     5. Parse \operatorname{out}_1 = \operatorname{out}_2 = [\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}
      6. Abort if \Phi_{\mathsf{valid}}([\mathbf{z}_i, \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}) = 0, where [\mathbf{z}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*} are the input instances in inst
      7. Return [\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}
```

<span id="page-29-3"></span><span id="page-29-2"></span><span id="page-29-1"></span><span id="page-29-0"></span>Figure 4: The extractor for  $\Pi_{\text{fold}}$  using the validity predicate  $\Phi_{\text{valid}}$  from (18).

vectors  $[\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*} \in (\mathcal{R}_q^m)^{k^*}$ , and  $i \in [k^*]$ , define the multilinear polynomial

<span id="page-30-1"></span>
$$p_i(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) := \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}} eq(\vec{\mathbf{x}}, \vec{\mathbf{b}}) \cdot \prod_{j=1-b}^{b-1} \left( \mathsf{mle} \left[ \hat{\mathbf{f}}_i \right] (\vec{\mathbf{b}}) - j \right). \tag{17}$$

Note that  $p_i(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) = 0$  implies that  $\prod_{j=1-b}^{b-1} \left( \mathsf{mle} \left[ \hat{\mathbf{f}}_i \right] (\vec{\mathbf{b}}) - j \right) = 0$  for every  $\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}$ , which in turn implies  $\|\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i\|_{\infty} < b$  from the discussion in Section 3.1. The predicate  $\Phi_{\mathsf{valid}}([\mathbf{z}_i, \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*})$  is true if and only if

<span id="page-30-0"></span>
$$\forall i \in [k^*] : \left( \mathsf{mle} \left[ \hat{\mathbf{f}}_i \right] (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i) = \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i \right) \wedge \left( \mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i) = \mathbf{y}_i \right) \wedge \left( p_i(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) = 0 \right). \tag{18}$$

Hence,  $\Phi_{\mathsf{valid}}([\mathbf{z}_i, \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}) = 1$  if and only if  $[\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}$  are valid witnesses for  $[\mathbf{z}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}$ , that is,  $[\mathbf{z}_i, \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*} \in (\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{hom}}^b)^{k^*}$ . Thus, given the check at Step 6, the extractor always outputs a valid witness if it does not abort.

Running time. We adapt the proof of Lemma 7.1 in [FMN23] to analyze the expected running time of the extractor. We first analyze the expected running time of each execution of SubExt<sup>P\*</sup>. Fix any input (inst,  $\psi$ ), we denote by  $C_0 := (\Sigma_1, \ldots, \Sigma_{k^*})$  the random variable for the folding challenges  $c_0 := (\rho_1, \ldots, \rho_{k^*})$ . We define event  $\Gamma := (P^*(\text{inst}, C_0, \psi) \neq \bot)$ .

Let T be the number of calls to  $\mathsf{P}^*$  in  $\mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst}, \psi)$ . For  $i \in [k^*]$ , let  $T_i$  be the number of calls to  $\mathsf{P}^*$  made during the i-th iteration of the loop. We have  $\mathbb{E}[T] = 1 + \sum_{i=1}^{k^*} \mathbb{E}[T_i]$  by linearity of expectation.

Define the random variable

$$X_i := \left| \left\{ x \in \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}} : \mathsf{P}^*(\mathsf{inst}, C(x), \psi) \neq \bot \right\} \right| \tag{19}$$

where  $C(x) := (\Sigma_1, \dots, \Sigma_{i-1}, x, \Sigma_{i+1}, \dots, \Sigma_{k^*})$ . Let  $N := |\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}|$ , we have that

$$\mathbb{E}[T_i] = \sum_{j=0}^{N} \mathbb{E}[T_i \mid X_i = j] \cdot \Pr[X_i = j].$$

Also note that  $T_i = 0$  when  $\Gamma = 0$ , thus for any  $j \geq 0$ , we have that

$$\mathbb{E}[T_i|X_i=j] = \Pr[\Gamma=1 \mid X_i=j] \cdot \mathbb{E}[T_i \mid (\Gamma=1) \land X_i=j]$$

where  $\Pr[\Gamma = 1 \mid X_i = j] = j/N$  and  $\mathbb{E}[T_i \mid (\Gamma = 1) \land X_i = j]$  is the expectation of a negative hypergeometric distribution, that is, challenges  $\rho'_i$  are drawn without replacement from a set of size N-1 that contains j-1 correct responses. Hence,  $\mathbb{E}[T_i \mid (\Gamma = 1) \land X_i = j] \leq N/j$ 

and therefore  $\mathbb{E}[T_i|X_i=j] \leq j/N \cdot (N/j) = 1$ . In sum, for all  $i \in [k^*]$ , we have that  $\mathbb{E}[T_i] \leq \sum_{j=0}^N 1 \cdot \Pr[X_i=j] = 1$ , and therefore

<span id="page-31-0"></span>
$$\mathbb{E}[T] = 1 + \sum_{i=1}^{k^*} \mathbb{E}[T_i] \le 1 + k^*.$$

Next, we analyze the success probability of each independent run of  $\mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}$ . Since  $\mathcal{A}$ ,  $\mathsf{P}^*$  are deterministic, we have that the event  $\Gamma := (\mathsf{P}^*(\mathsf{inst}, C_0, \psi) \neq \bot)$  happens with probability  $\epsilon_{\mathsf{fold}}(\mathcal{A}, \mathsf{P}^*)$  over the randomness of  $\psi$  and  $C_0$ . Define E as the event that a fresh call of  $\mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst}, \psi)$  does not return  $\bot$ . We have that

$$\Pr[E] = \Pr[\Gamma = 1 \land (\land_{i=1}^{k^*} X_i \ge 2)]$$

$$= \Pr[\Gamma = 1] - \Pr[\Gamma = 1 \land (\lor_{i=1}^{k^*} X_i = 1)]$$

$$\ge \Pr[\Gamma = 1] - \sum_{i=1}^{k^*} \Pr[\Gamma = 1 \land X_i = 1]$$

$$\ge \Pr[\Gamma = 1] - \frac{k^*}{|\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}|}$$

$$\ge \epsilon_{\mathsf{fold}}(\mathcal{A}, \mathsf{P}^*) - \frac{k^*}{|\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}|}.$$
(20)

In sum, the expected number of calls to P\* in the extractor is at most  $(\mathbb{E}[T]/\Pr[E])+E[T] = \left(1+1/\left(\epsilon_{\mathsf{fold}}(\mathcal{A},\mathsf{P}^*)-\frac{2k}{|\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}|}\right)\right)\cdot(1+2k) = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda).$ 

**Success probability.** Towards analyzing the extractor's success probability, we define the following events.

- $E_{\text{ext}}$ : the extractor recovers the witnesses  $\text{out}_1, \text{out}_2 \neq \bot$ , and,  $\text{out}_1 = \text{out}_2$ .
- $E_{\mathsf{valid}}$ :  $E_{\mathsf{ext}}$  occurs and the extracted witness is valid, i.e.,  $\Phi_{\mathsf{valid}}([\mathbf{x}_i, \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}) = 1$  for the input instances  $[\mathbf{x}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}$  and the interpolated witness  $[\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}$ .

 $E_{\mathsf{ext}} \wedge E_{\mathsf{valid}}$  implies that the extractor returns a valid witness for the input instances. Moreover,

$$\Pr[E_{\mathsf{ext}} \wedge E_{\mathsf{valid}}] = \Pr[E_{\mathsf{ext}}] - \Pr[E_{\mathsf{ext}} \wedge \overline{E_{\mathsf{valid}}}],$$

thus it suffices to lower-bound  $\Pr[E_{\mathsf{ext}}]$  and upper-bound  $\Pr[E_{\mathsf{ext}} \wedge \overline{E_{\mathsf{valid}}}]$ .

Claim 1. 
$$\Pr[E_{\mathsf{ext}}] \ge \epsilon_{\mathsf{fold}}(\mathcal{A}, \mathsf{P}^*) - \frac{k^*}{|\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}|} - \epsilon_{\mathsf{bind}}$$

*Proof.* We define  $E'_{\text{ext}}$  as the event that the last call of  $\text{SubExt}^{P^*}$ , on input (inst,  $\psi'$ ), does not return  $\bot$ . By Eq. (20), we have that

$$\Pr[E'_{\mathsf{ext}}] \ge \epsilon_{\mathsf{fold}}(\mathcal{A}, \mathsf{P}^*) - \frac{k^*}{|\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}|}$$

because (i)  $\mathcal{A}$  is deterministic, and (ii)  $\psi'$  and the randomness in  $\mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst}, \psi')$  are freshly sampled.

Suppose  $E'_{\text{ext}}$  occurs. Let  $(\mathsf{open}_1, \mathsf{out}_1)$ ,  $(\mathsf{open}_2, \mathsf{out}_2)$  be the output of  $\mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst}, \psi)$  and  $\mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst}, \psi')$  respectively. We next show that  $\mathsf{out}_1 = \mathsf{out}_2$  (and thus  $E_{\mathsf{ext}}$  holds) with high probability. For every  $i \in [k^*]$ , let  $\mathsf{open}_{1,i} := (\Delta, \vec{\mathbf{w}})$  and  $\mathsf{open}_{2,i} := (\Delta', \vec{\mathbf{w}}')$ . Recall the assumption that  $\mathsf{P}^*$  produces an output only when the witness is valid for the folded instance. Therefore, the interpolated witnesses  $\vec{\mathbf{w}}$ ,  $\vec{\mathbf{w}}'$  output by  $\mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}$  must satisfy that  $\mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{w}}) = \Delta y_i$  and  $\mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{w}}') = \Delta' y_i$ . Suppose for contradiction that  $\mathsf{out}_{1,i} = \Delta^{-1}\vec{\mathbf{w}} \neq (\Delta')^{-1}\vec{\mathbf{w}}' = \mathsf{out}_{2,i}$ , then  $\Delta'\vec{\mathbf{w}} \neq \Delta\vec{\mathbf{w}}'$ , and  $(\mathsf{open}_{1,i}, \mathsf{open}_{2,i})$  is a pair of distinct 2B-weak openings that breaks the 2B-relaxed binding property of  $\mathcal{L}$ . Specifically,  $\mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{w}}) = \Delta y_i$  and  $\mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{w}}') = \Delta' y_i$ ;  $\|\vec{\mathbf{w}}\|_{\infty}$ ,  $\|\vec{\mathbf{w}}'\|_{\infty} < 2B$  because  $\vec{\mathbf{w}}$  and  $\vec{\mathbf{w}}'$  are the subtractions of two vectors with norm less than B; and  $\Delta$ ,  $\Delta'$  are non-zero differences in the set  $\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}$ . Moreover, the extractor is an expected polynomial time algorithm. Thus, by the relaxed binding property of  $\mathcal{L}$ , we have that

$$\Pr\left[E'_{\mathsf{ext}} \land (\mathsf{out}_1 \neq \mathsf{out}_2)\right] \leq \epsilon_{\mathsf{bind}} \,.$$

Therefore, we have that

$$\begin{split} \Pr[E_{\mathsf{ext}}] &= \Pr[E'_{\mathsf{ext}}] - \Pr\left[E'_{\mathsf{ext}} \wedge (\mathsf{out}_1 \neq \mathsf{out}_2)\right] \\ &\geq \Pr[E'_{\mathsf{ext}}] - \epsilon_{\mathsf{bind}} \\ &\geq \epsilon_{\mathsf{fold}}(\mathcal{A}, \mathsf{P}^*) - \frac{k^*}{|\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}|} - \epsilon_{\mathsf{bind}} \,, \end{split}$$

which completes the proof.

Next, we upper-bound the probability of  $E_{\text{ext}} \wedge \overline{E_{\text{valid}}}$  – the event that extractor recovers witnesses  $\text{out}_1 = \text{out}_2$  but the extracted witness is invalid.

We first reduce  $\Pr[E_{\mathsf{ext}} \wedge \overline{E_{\mathsf{valid}}}]$  to the probability of a different event that is easier to analyze. Let inst denote  $\mathcal{A}$ 's output that includes the input instances  $[\mathbf{z}_i := (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, y_i)]_{i=1}^{k^*}$ . Let  $\psi' := ([\alpha'_i, \mu'_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}, \vec{\beta}', \vec{\mathbf{r}}'_o)$  be the last sampled randomness. We consider the sub-extraction call  $\mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst}, \psi')$ : Let  $c_0 := (\rho_1, \dots, \rho_{k^*})$  denote the initial folding challenge, and let  $[\theta'_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}$  denote the claimed evaluations in the transcript of  $\mathsf{P}^*(\mathsf{inst}, c_0, \psi')$ . Let  $[\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}$  denote the interpolated vectors when  $E_{\mathsf{ext}}$  occurs, and let  $[p_i(\vec{\mathbf{x}})]_{i=1}^{k^*}$  be the corresponding

polynomials specified in Eq. (17). Define events  $E_{\text{hom}}$ ,  $E_{\text{eval}}$ ,  $E_{\text{bad}}$  as

<span id="page-33-0"></span>
$$E_{\mathsf{hom}} := E_{\mathsf{ext}} \wedge (\forall i \in [k^*] : \mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i) = y_i), \qquad (21)$$

$$E_{\text{eval}} := E_{\text{ext}} \wedge (\forall i \in [k^*] : \text{mle} \left[ \hat{\mathbf{f}}_i \right] (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o') = \theta_i'), \qquad (22)$$

<span id="page-33-2"></span><span id="page-33-1"></span>
$$E_{\mathsf{bad}} := E_{\mathsf{ext}} \land (\exists i \in [k^*] : \left(\mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i) \neq \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i\right) \lor (p_i(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) \neq 0)). \tag{23}$$

Informally,  $E_{\text{eval}}$  implies that the reduced evaluation claim holds after running the sumcheck;  $E_{\text{bad}}$  implies that the extracted witness is invalid.

<span id="page-33-3"></span>Claim 2. 
$$\Pr[E_{\mathsf{ext}} \wedge \overline{E_{\mathsf{valid}}}] = \Pr[E_{\mathsf{eval}} \wedge E_{\mathsf{bad}}].$$

*Proof.* Assume that  $E_{\mathsf{ext}} \Longrightarrow (E_{\mathsf{hom}} \land E_{\mathsf{eval}})$  holds (which we will prove later), we argue that  $E_{\mathsf{ext}} \land \overline{E_{\mathsf{valid}}}$  occurs if and only if  $E_{\mathsf{eval}} \land E_{\mathsf{bad}}$  occurs.

We recall the definitions of  $E_{\text{ext}}$ ,  $E_{\text{valid}}$ ,  $E_{\text{hom}}$  (Eq. (21)),  $E_{\text{eval}}$  (Eq. (22)) and  $E_{\text{bad}}$  (Eq. (23)). Informally,  $E_{\text{ext}}$  means that the witnesses  $\text{out}_1$ ,  $\text{out}_2 \neq \bot$  recovered by the extractor are the same.  $E_{\text{valid}}$  means that the recovered witness is valid.  $E_{\text{hom}}$  means that the interpolated witness satisfies the homomorphism relation, i.e.,  $\mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i) = y_i$  for every  $i \in [k^*]$ .  $E_{\text{eval}}$  means that the reduced evaluation checks (after sumcheck) pass for the interpolated witness, i.e.,  $\text{mle } \left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o') = \theta_i'$  for every  $i \in [k^*]$ . Finally,  $E_{\text{bad}}$  means that the input evaluation claims or the norm constraint do not hold for the interpolated witness.

Suppose  $E_{\mathsf{ext}} \wedge \overline{E_{\mathsf{valid}}}$  occurs. By the assumption that  $E_{\mathsf{ext}} \Longrightarrow (E_{\mathsf{hom}} \wedge E_{\mathsf{eval}})$  holds,  $E_{\mathsf{eval}}$  and  $E_{\mathsf{hom}}$  must also occur. Moreover, if  $E_{\mathsf{hom}}$  occurs while  $E_{\mathsf{valid}}$  does not, it must be the case that  $E_{\mathsf{bad}}$  occurs. Therefore,  $E_{\mathsf{eval}} \wedge E_{\mathsf{bad}}$  will occur.

Conversely, suppose  $E_{\text{eval}} \wedge E_{\text{bad}}$  occurs. Then  $E_{\text{ext}}$  certainly occurs. However,  $E_{\text{valid}}$  cannot occur because  $E_{\text{bad}}$  occurs, and thus  $E_{\text{ext}} \wedge \overline{E_{\text{valid}}}$  occurs.

Now it suffices to show that  $E_{\mathsf{ext}} \Longrightarrow (E_{\mathsf{hom}} \land E_{\mathsf{eval}})$ . Suppose  $E_{\mathsf{ext}}$  occurs. Let  $[c_i, \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i]_{i=0}^{k^*}$  denote the tuples collected in  $\mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst}, \psi')$  where  $c_0 := (\rho_1, \dots, \rho_{k^*})$  and

$$c_i := (\rho_1, \dots, \rho_{i-1}, \rho'_i, \rho_{i+1}, \dots, \rho_{k^*}).$$

For every  $i \in [k^*]$ , since  $\vec{\mathbf{w}}_0, \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i \neq \bot$  are valid witnesses, we have that

$$\mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{w}}_0) = \rho_1 y_1 + \dots + \rho_{i-1} y_{i-1} + \rho_i y_i + \rho_{i+1} y_{i+1} + \dots + \rho_{k^*} y_{k^*},$$
  

$$\mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{w}}_i) = \rho_1 y_1 + \dots + \rho_{i-1} y_{i-1} + \rho_i' y_i + \rho_{i+1} y_{i+1} + \dots + \rho_{k^*} y_{k^*},$$

thus

$$\mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i) = \mathcal{L}((\vec{\mathbf{w}}_0 - \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i) \cdot (\rho_i - \rho_i')^{-1})$$

$$= (\rho_i - \rho_i')^{-1} \cdot \mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{w}}_0 - \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i)$$

$$= (\rho_i - \rho_i')^{-1} \cdot (\mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{w}}_0) - \mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{w}}_i))$$

$$= (\rho_i - \rho_i')^{-1} \cdot (\rho_i - \rho_i') \cdot y_i = y_i,$$

which implies that  $E_{\mathsf{hom}}$  occurs.

Similarly, since the prover  $\mathsf{P}^*$  needs to output  $[\theta'_j]_{j=1}^{k^*}$  before receiving the folding challenges, the claimed evaluations  $\{\theta'_j\}$  in the executions of  $\mathsf{P}^*(\mathsf{inst}, c_0, \psi')$  and  $\mathsf{P}^*(\mathsf{inst}, c_i, \psi')$  are the same. Define

$$\hat{\mathbf{v}}_{o}^{(0)} := \mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{w}}_{0}\right]\left(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_{o}'\right), \qquad \hat{\mathbf{v}}_{o}^{(i)} := \mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{w}}_{i}\right]\left(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_{o}'\right).$$

Note that

$$\mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{v}}_o^{(0)}) := \mathsf{mle}\left[\mathsf{Coef}(\vec{\mathbf{w}}_0)\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o')\,, \qquad \mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{v}}_o^{(i)}) := \mathsf{mle}\left[\mathsf{Coef}(\vec{\mathbf{w}}_i)\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o')\,.$$

Since P\* outputs valid witnesses for the output instances, we have that

$$\begin{split} & \mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{v}}_o^{(0)}) = \sum_{j=1}^{k^*} \mathsf{RotSum}(\rho_j, \mathsf{NTT}(\theta_j')) \,, \\ & \mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{v}}_o^{(i)}) = \sum_{j \in [k^*], j \neq i} \mathsf{RotSum}(\rho_j, \mathsf{NTT}(\theta_j')) + \mathsf{RotSum}(\rho_i', \mathsf{NTT}(\theta_i')) \,, \end{split}$$

which implies that

<span id="page-34-0"></span>
$$\mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{v}}_{o}^{(0)} - \hat{\mathbf{v}}_{o}^{(i)}) = \mathsf{RotSum}(\rho_{i}, \mathsf{NTT}(\theta_{i}')) - \mathsf{RotSum}(\rho_{i}', \mathsf{NTT}(\theta_{i}')). \tag{24}$$

Let  $\Delta_o$ ,  $\bar{\theta}'_i$  be the values such that  $\mathsf{Coef}(\Delta_o) = \mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{v}}_o^{(0)} - \hat{\mathbf{v}}_o^{(i)})$  and  $\mathsf{Coef}(\bar{\theta}'_i) = \mathsf{NTT}(\theta'_i)$ . By Lemma 2.1, we have that

$$\mathsf{RotSum}(\rho_i,\mathsf{NTT}(\theta_i')) = \mathsf{Coef}(\rho_i \cdot \bar{\theta}_i')\,, \qquad \mathsf{RotSum}(\rho_i',\mathsf{NTT}(\theta_i')) = \mathsf{Coef}(\rho_i' \cdot \bar{\theta}_i')\,.$$

Then by Eq. (24), we have that  $\mathsf{Coef}(\Delta_o) = \mathsf{Coef}((\rho_i - \rho_i') \cdot \bar{\theta}_i')$  and thus  $\mathsf{Coef}((\rho_i - \rho_i')^{-1} \cdot \Delta_o) = \mathsf{Coef}(\bar{\theta}_i')$ . By definition of  $\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i$ , we have that

$$\begin{split} \operatorname{mle}\left[\operatorname{Coef}(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i)\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o') &= \operatorname{mle}\left[\operatorname{Coef}((\vec{\mathbf{w}}_0 - \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i) \cdot (\rho_i - \rho_i')^{-1})\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o') \\ &= (\rho_i - \rho_i')^{-1} \cdot \operatorname{mle}\left[\operatorname{Coef}(\vec{\mathbf{w}}_0 - \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i)\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o') \\ &= (\rho_i - \rho_i')^{-1} \cdot \left(\operatorname{mle}\left[\operatorname{Coef}(\vec{\mathbf{w}}_0)\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o') - \operatorname{mle}\left[\operatorname{Coef}(\vec{\mathbf{w}}_i)\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o')\right) \\ &= (\rho_i - \rho_i')^{-1} \cdot \left(\operatorname{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{v}}_o^{(0)}) - \operatorname{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{v}}_o^{(i)})\right) \\ &= (\rho_i - \rho_i')^{-1} \cdot \operatorname{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{v}}_o^{(0)} - \hat{\mathbf{v}}_o^{(i)}) \\ &= (\rho_i - \rho_i')^{-1} \cdot \operatorname{Coef}(\Delta_o) \\ &= \operatorname{Coef}((\rho_i - \rho_i')^{-1} \cdot \Delta_o) \\ &= \operatorname{Coef}(\vec{\theta}_i') = \operatorname{NTT}(\theta_i') \,. \end{split}$$

By Lemma A.1 and because  $\mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i) = \mathsf{Coef}(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i)$ , this implies that  $\mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o') = \theta_i'$ . Therefore,  $E_{\mathsf{eval}}$  occurs, which finishes the proof.

<span id="page-35-0"></span>Therefore, to analyze  $\Pr[E_{\mathsf{ext}} \wedge \overline{E_{\mathsf{valid}}}]$ , it suffices to analyze the probability of  $E_{\mathsf{eval}} \wedge E_{\mathsf{bad}}$ . **Lemma 3.7.**  $\Pr[E_{\mathsf{eval}} \wedge E_{\mathsf{bad}}] \leq \frac{(2b+1)\log m + 2k^*}{|\mathcal{C}|}$ .

Proof. Let  $[\mathbf{x}_i := (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, \mathbf{y}_i)]_{i=1}^{k^*}$  and  $[\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}$  denote the input instances and the extracted witness vectors, respectively. For every  $i \in [k^*]$ , let  $p_i(\vec{\mathbf{x}})$  denote the multilinear polynomial specified in Eq. (17), with respect to  $\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i$ . Let  $\psi' := ([\alpha'_i, \mu'_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}, \vec{\beta}', \vec{\mathbf{r}}'_o)$  be the input randomness used in the last call SubExt<sup>P\*</sup>(inst,  $\psi'$ ), namely on line 4 of the extractor. Define polynomial h as

<span id="page-35-1"></span>
$$h([X_i, Y_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}) := \sum_{i=1}^{k^*} \left( \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i - \mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right] (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i) \right) \cdot X_i + \sum_{i=1}^{k^*} p_i(\vec{\beta}') \cdot Y_i.$$
 (25)

We define the following events:

$$\begin{split} E_1 &:= E_{\text{ext}} \wedge (\exists i \in [k^*] : p_i(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) \neq 0) \wedge \left( p_i(\vec{\beta}') = 0 \forall i \in [k^*] \right) \\ E_2 &:= E_{\text{ext}} \wedge \left( h([\alpha_i', \mu_i']_{i=1}^{k^*}) = 0 \right) \wedge \left( \exists i \in [k^*] : \left( \text{mle} \left[ \hat{\mathbf{f}}_i \right] (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i) \neq \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i \right) \vee \left( p_i(\vec{\beta}') \neq 0 \right) \right) \\ E_3 &:= E_{\text{eval}} \wedge \left( h([\alpha_i', \mu_i']_{i=1}^{k^*}) \neq 0 \right) \end{split}$$

Intuitively, we "split" the event  $E_{\text{eval}} \wedge E_{\text{bad}}$  into three parts  $E_1$ ,  $E_2$ ,  $E_3$ , so that we can reduce  $\Pr[E_{\text{eval}} \wedge E_{\text{bad}}]$  to the probability of breaking sumcheck soundness. In particular,  $E_3$  implies that the reduced evaluation claim holds (i.e.,  $E_{\text{eval}}$  holds), while the sumcheck claim is false (i.e.,  $h([\alpha'_i, \mu'_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}) \neq 0$ ).

We first show that  $(E_{\mathsf{eval}} \wedge E_{\mathsf{bad}}) \implies (E_1 \vee E_2 \vee E_3)$ . Note that  $E_{\mathsf{eval}} \wedge E_{\mathsf{bad}}$  implies that  $E_{\mathsf{ext}}$  occurs and  $[\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}$  are well-defined. Moreover, if  $E_1$  doesn't occur, then  $\overline{E_1} \wedge E_{\mathsf{bad}}$  occurs, that is,

$$\exists i \in [k^*] \; : \; \left( \mathsf{mle} \left[ \hat{\mathbf{f}}_i \right] (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i) \neq \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i \right) \vee \left( p_i(\vec{\beta}') \neq 0 \right),$$

which implies that  $E_2 \vee E_3$  occurs. Thus,  $(E_{\text{eval}} \wedge E_{\text{bad}}) \implies (E_1 \vee E_2 \vee E_3)$  and

$$\Pr[E_{\mathsf{eval}} \land E_{\mathsf{bad}}] \le \Pr[E_1 \lor E_2 \lor E_3] \le \Pr[E_1] + \Pr[E_2] + \Pr[E_3]. \tag{26}$$

Now, it suffices to bound the probabilities  $Pr[E_1]$ ,  $Pr[E_2]$ ,  $Pr[E_3]$ .

Claim 3.  $\Pr[E_1] \leq \log m/|\mathcal{C}|$ .

*Proof.* Consider a mental experiment  $\mathsf{Exp}_1$  that simulates  $\mathsf{Ext}^{\mathcal{A},\mathsf{P}^*}$  until Step 3.  $\mathsf{Exp}_1$  outputs 1 if and only if

$$(\exists i \in [k^*] : p_i(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) \neq 0) \land (p_i(\vec{\beta}') = 0 \forall i \in [k^*])$$

where  $[p_i(\vec{\mathbf{x}})]_{i=1}^{k^*}$  are derived from  $[\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}$  output by  $\mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst}, \psi)$ . It is clear that  $\Pr[\mathsf{Exp}_1 = 1] \geq \Pr[E_1]$ . Moreover, let  $i^* \in [k^*]$  be the first index such that  $p_{i^*}(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) \neq 0$ . Since

 $[\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}$  in  $\mathsf{Exp}_1$  is independent of  $\psi'$ , by the Generalized Schwartz Lemma (Lemma 2.4), the probability that  $p_{i^*}(\vec{\beta}') = 0$  is at most  $\frac{\log m}{|\mathcal{C}|}$  (over the randomness  $\vec{\beta}'$ ). Thus  $\Pr[E_1] \leq \Pr[\mathsf{Exp}_1 = 1] \leq \frac{\log m}{|\mathcal{C}|}$ .

Claim 4.  $\Pr[E_2] \leq 2k^*/|C|$ .

*Proof.* Consider a mental experiment  $\mathsf{Exp}_2$  that that simulates  $\mathsf{Ext}^{\mathcal{A},\mathsf{P}^*}$  until Step 3.  $\mathsf{Exp}_2$  outputs 1 if and only if

$$\left(h([\alpha_i',\mu_i']_{i=1}^{k^*})=0\right)\wedge\left(\exists i\in[k^*]\ :\ \left(\mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i)\neq\hat{\mathbf{v}}_i\right)\vee\left(p_i(\vec{\beta}')\neq0\right)\right)$$

where h is specified in Eq. (25), and  $[p_i(\vec{\mathbf{x}})]_{i=1}^{k^*}$  are defined given the witness  $[\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}$  derived from SubExt<sup>P\*</sup>(inst,  $\psi$ ). It is clear that  $\Pr[\mathsf{Exp}_2 = 1] \geq \Pr[E_2]$ . Moreover, since  $[\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}$  in  $\mathsf{Exp}_2$  is independent of  $\psi'$ , by the Generalized Schwartz Lemma (Lemma 2.4), the probability that  $h([\alpha_i', \mu_i']_{i=1}^{k^*}) = 0$  is at most  $\frac{2k^*}{|\mathcal{C}|}$  (over the choice of  $[\alpha_i', \mu_i']_{i=1}^{k^*}$ ). Thus  $\Pr[E_2] \leq \Pr[\mathsf{Exp}_2 = 1] \leq \frac{2k^*}{|\mathcal{C}|}$ .

Claim 5.  $\Pr[E_3] \leq 2b \log m/|\mathcal{C}|$ .

*Proof.* Consider a mental experiment  $\mathsf{Exp}_3$  that simulates  $\mathsf{Ext}^{\mathcal{A},\mathsf{P}^*}$  until Step 3. Additionally, it simulates  $\mathsf{P}^*(\mathsf{inst},\bot,\psi')$  to obtain claimed evaluations  $\{\theta'_j\}$  in the partial transcript without providing folding challenges.  $\mathsf{Exp}_3$  outputs 1 if and only if the verification at Step 4 passes and

$$\left(h([\alpha_i',\mu_i']_{i=1}^{k^*}) \neq 0\right) \wedge \left(\forall i \in [k^*] \ : \ \mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o') = \theta_i'\right),$$

where h is specified in Eq. (25) and  $[\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}$  are obtained from  $\mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst}, \psi)$ .

We show that  $\Pr[\mathsf{Exp}_3 = 1] \geq \Pr[E_3]$ . Recall that  $E_3$  implies that  $E_{\mathsf{ext}}$  occurs, which implies that  $[\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}$  computed from  $\mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst}, \psi)$  is **identical** to that from  $\mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst}, \psi')$ . Moreover,  $E_3$  implies that  $E_{\mathsf{eval}}$  occurs, i.e., the evaluation check in the execution  $\mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst}, \psi')$  passes. Since the witness  $[\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}$  extracted from  $\mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst}, \psi')$  is the same as that from  $\mathsf{SubExt}^{\mathsf{P}^*}(\mathsf{inst}, \psi)$ , we have that  $\mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o') = \theta_i'$  for all  $i \in [k^*]$ . Therefore, with the same randomness, if  $E_3$  happens, then  $\mathsf{Exp}_3$  will output 1. Thus  $\mathsf{Pr}[\mathsf{Exp}_3 = 1] \geq \mathsf{Pr}[E_3]$ .

Now, it suffices to bound  $\Pr[\mathsf{Exp}_3 = 1]$ . For every  $i \in [k^*]$ , we define  $p_i(\vec{\mathbf{x}})$  from  $\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i$  according to Eq. (17). We can rewrite  $p_i(\vec{\beta}')$  as

<span id="page-36-0"></span>
$$p_{i}(\vec{\beta}') = \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}} eq(\vec{\beta}', \vec{\mathbf{b}}) \cdot \prod_{j=1-b}^{b-1} \left( \mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_{i}\right](\vec{\mathbf{b}}) - j \right) = \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}} g_{2,i}(\vec{\mathbf{b}}), \qquad (27)$$

where  $g_{2,i}$  is specified in Eq. (16). Similarly, we can rewrite  $\mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i)$  as

<span id="page-36-1"></span>
$$\operatorname{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_{i}\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_{i}) = \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}} eq(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_{i}, \vec{\mathbf{b}}) \cdot \operatorname{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_{i}\right](\vec{\mathbf{b}}) = \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}} g_{1,i}(\vec{\mathbf{b}}), \tag{28}$$

where  $g_{1,i}$  is specified in Eq. (15). Recall that g in Eq. (14) is defined as

$$g(\vec{\mathbf{b}}) := \sum_{i=1}^{k^*} \left[ \alpha_i' g_{1,i}(\vec{\mathbf{b}}) + \mu_i' g_{2,i}(\vec{\mathbf{b}}) \right].$$

By plugging-in Eq. (27) and Eq. (28), we have that

$$\sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}} g(\vec{\mathbf{b}}) = \sum_{i=1}^{k^*} \alpha_i' \cdot \mathsf{mle} \left[ \hat{\mathbf{f}}_i \right] (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i) + \sum_{i=1}^{k^*} \mu_i' \cdot p_i(\vec{\beta}'). \tag{29}$$

Therefore, the sumcheck statement

$$\sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}} g(\vec{\mathbf{b}}) = \sum_{i=1}^{k^*} \alpha_i \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i$$

holds if and only if  $h([\alpha'_i, \mu'_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}) = 0$ . Recall that  $\mathsf{Exp}_3 = 1$  implies that  $h([\alpha'_i, \mu'_i]_{i=1}^{k^*}) \neq 0$ , i.e., the sumcheck statement does not hold. Meanwhile, note that the random evaluation statement for g holds because

$$\forall i \in [k^*] : \mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o') = \theta_i'$$

and the verification at Step 4 passes. By the Generalized Sum-Check Theorem (Lemma 2.5),  $\Pr[E_3] \leq \Pr[\mathsf{Exp}_3] \leq 2b \log m/|\mathcal{C}|$  (over the randomness of  $\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o'$ ).

In summary, we have that

$$\Pr[E_{\mathsf{eval}} \land E_{\mathsf{bad}}] \le \Pr[E_1] + \Pr[E_2] + \Pr[E_3] \le \frac{\log m}{|\mathcal{C}|} + \frac{2k^*}{|\mathcal{C}|} + \frac{2b \log m}{|\mathcal{C}|},$$

which finishes the proof of Lemma 3.7.

Thus, the success probability of the extractor is at least

$$\Pr[E_{\mathsf{ext}} \land E_{\mathsf{valid}}] \ge \epsilon_{\mathsf{fold}}(\mathcal{A}, \mathsf{P}^*) - \frac{k^*}{|\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}|} - \epsilon_{\mathsf{bind}} - \frac{(2b+1)\log m + 2k^*}{|\mathcal{C}|},$$

which finishes the proof of Theorem 3.3.

Remark 3.3. Theorem 3.3 is applicable only when  $\Pi_{\mathsf{fold}}$  is instantiated as an interactive protocol. In practice,  $\Pi_{\mathsf{fold}}$  can be converted into a non-interactive protocol using the Fiat-Shamir transform. The knowledge analysis of the Fiat-Shamir transformed version of  $\Pi_{\mathsf{fold}}$  is left as future work.

#### <span id="page-38-0"></span>3.3 Supporting Small Prime Modulus

In the protocol  $\Pi_{\mathsf{fold}}$  (Figure 3), if  $\mathcal{R}_q \cong \mathbb{Z}_q^d$ , the size of the strong sampling set  $\mathcal{C} := \mathbb{Z}_q$  is only q. This is the best we can hope for: Assume for contradiction that exists  $\mathcal{C}$  where  $|\mathcal{C}| > q$ , by the pigeonhole principle, there exist two elements  $\mathbf{a}, \mathbf{b}$  in  $\mathcal{C} \subseteq \mathcal{R}_q \cong \mathbb{Z}_q^d$  that share the same value at the 1st slot of their NTT representation. Hence the 1st slot of NTT( $\mathbf{a} - \mathbf{b}$ ) is zero, and  $\mathbf{a} - \mathbf{b}$  is a zero-divisor as  $\mathbf{c} \cdot (\mathbf{a} - \mathbf{b}) = 0$  for the element  $\mathbf{c} \neq 0$  whose NTT representation is  $(1, 0, \ldots, 0)$ . This contradicts with the fact that  $\mathcal{C}$  is a sampling set.

To achieve 128-bit security, we need to use at least a 128-bit prime modulus in  $\Pi_{\text{fold}}$ . In practice, however, it would be significantly more efficient to use a smaller modulus, say a 32-bit prime, which is a good fit for GPUs that operate on 32-bit data types, or for CPUs that operate on 32 or 64-bit integer types.

In this section, we describe an optimization that extends  $\Pi_{\mathsf{fold}}$  to support a small prime modulus q. The key idea is to use q where  $\mathcal{R}_q \cong \mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}^t$  for some  $\tau > 1$  such that  $q^{\tau} \approx 2^{128}$ . Here  $\mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}$  is an extension field of  $\mathbb{F}_q$ . We note, however, that q cannot be too small since we must preserve the hardness of the MSIS problem.

Let  $t \in \mathbb{N}$  be a divisor of d and denote  $\tau := d/t$ . Let q be a prime such that  $q \equiv 1 + 2t \pmod{4t}$  and  $q^{\tau} \approx 2^{128}$ . Recall from Section 2 that we have  $\mathcal{R}_q \cong \mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}^t$  via the NTT isomorphism. Thus we can rewrite the commitment opening relation  $\mathcal{R}_{cm}^B$  (Eq. (8)) as

$$\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{cm}}^{\tau,B} := \left\{ (\mathsf{pp}, \mathsf{cm} \in \mathcal{R}_q^\kappa; \vec{\mathbf{f}} \in \mathcal{R}_q^m) \ : \begin{array}{c} (\mathsf{cm} = \mathbf{A}\vec{\mathbf{f}}) \wedge \\ \forall j \in [\tau]: \\ \left(\hat{\mathbf{f}}_j \circ \left[ \bigcirc_{i=1}^{B-1} (\hat{\mathbf{f}}_j - \hat{i}) \circ (\hat{\mathbf{f}}_j + \hat{i}) \right] = \hat{0} \right) \end{array} \right\},$$

here  $\hat{\mathbf{f}} := (\hat{\mathbf{f}}_1, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{f}}_{\tau}) \in \mathcal{R}_q^{m \times \tau}$  is the vector such that

$$\mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{f}}) := (\mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{f}}_1), \dots, \mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{f}}_{\tau})) \in \mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}^{m \times d}$$

equals the coefficient embedding matrix of  $\vec{\mathbf{f}}$  (which is in  $\mathbb{Z}_q^{m \times d}$ ), that is,  $\mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{f}}) = \mathsf{Coef}(\vec{\mathbf{f}})$ . Given  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{cm}}^{\tau,B}$ , we can similarly generalize the expanded commitment opening relation  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{eval}}^B$  (Eq. (9)) to  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{eval}}^{\tau,B}$  defined as

$$\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{eval}}^{\tau,B} := \left\{ (\mathsf{pp}, (\vec{\mathbf{r}}, [\hat{\mathbf{v}}_j]_{j=1}^\tau, \mathsf{cm}) \in \mathcal{R}_q^{\log m} \times \mathcal{R}_q^\tau \times \mathcal{R}_q^\kappa; \vec{\mathbf{f}} \in \mathcal{R}_q^m) : \begin{array}{c} (\mathsf{pp}, \mathsf{cm}; \vec{\mathbf{f}}) \in \mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{cm}}^B \wedge \\ \left( \forall j \in [\tau] : \mathsf{mle} \left[ \hat{\mathbf{f}}_j \right] (\vec{\mathbf{r}}) = \hat{\mathbf{v}}_j \right) \end{array} \right\}, \tag{30}$$

The reduction of knowledge from  $(\mathcal{R}_{\text{eval}}^{\tau,b})^{2k}$  to  $\mathcal{R}_{\text{eval}}^{\tau,B}$  is almost identical to  $\Pi_{\text{fold}}$  (Figure 3) except for 2 modifications below.

• We define the challenge space  $C \subseteq \mathcal{R}_q$  as the set of elements whose NTT representation equals i multiplying the identity vector  $I_t := (1, \dots, 1) \in \mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}^t$  (where i is enumerated over  $\mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}$ ), that is,

<span id="page-38-1"></span>
$$\mathcal{C} := \left\{ \mathbf{a}_i \in \mathcal{R}_q : \mathsf{NTT}(\mathbf{a}_i) = i \cdot I_t \right\}_{i \in \mathbb{F}_{q^\tau}}. \tag{31}$$

This ensures that  $\mathcal{C}$  is a strong sampling set with size  $q^{\tau} \approx 2^{128}$ , because the difference of any two distinct elements in  $\mathcal{C}$  maps to  $a \cdot I_t$  for some a in  $\mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}^{\times}$  through the NTT isomorphism, which has inverse  $a^{-1} \cdot I_t$ . Thus we can achieve 128-bit security even if q is significantly smaller than  $2^{128}$  (given  $\tau$  is large enough so that  $q^{\tau} \approx 2^{128}$ ).

• We argue that all proofs in Section 3.2 will still be valid. Let  $[\rho_i]_{i=1}^{2k}$  be the last folding challenges (in Figure 3). For every  $i \in [2k]$ , let  $\Theta_i := [\theta_{i,j}]_{j=1}^{\tau} \in \mathcal{R}_q^{\tau}$  where  $\{\theta_{i,j} \in \mathcal{R}_q\}$  are the claimed evaluations in the protocol execution. We denote by  $\mathsf{NTT}(\Theta_i) := (\mathsf{NTT}(\theta_{i,1}), \ldots, \mathsf{NTT}(\theta_{i,\tau})) \in \mathbb{F}_q^{d_{\tau}}$ . The folding verifier computes  $\hat{V}_o := [\hat{\mathbf{v}}_{o,j}]_{i=1}^{\tau} \in \mathcal{R}_q^{\tau}$  such that  $\mathsf{NTT}(\hat{V}_o) \in \mathbb{F}_q^{d_{\tau}}$  satisfies that

<span id="page-39-1"></span>
$$\mathsf{NTT}(\hat{V}_o) = \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \mathsf{RotSum}(\rho_i, \mathsf{NTT}(\Theta_i)), \qquad (32)$$

where RotSum is defined in Lemma 2.1. Therefore, by Lemma A.1, we can extend Lemma 3.2 to the case where  $\mathcal{R}_q \cong \mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}^{d/\tau}$  and the folding verifier can still verify the folding proof. Moreover, by the 3rd claim in Lemma 2.1, we can extend Eq. (24) to a more general setting where  $\mathcal{R}_q \cong \mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}^{d/\tau}$ . In this setting, the single linear equation (over  $\mathcal{R}_q$ ) in Eq. (24) is extended to  $\tau$  linear equations. Given this extension, all proofs in Section 3.2 naturally follow.

## <span id="page-39-0"></span>4 A Lattice-based Folding Scheme for CCS

In this section, we construct a folding scheme for customizable constraint systems (CCS) as introduced in [STW23a]. CCS is a generalization of Rank-1 Constraint Systems (R1CS) that supports high-degree custom gates, enabling better expressiveness and applicability. As discussed at the beginning of Section 3, this folding scheme enables us to build IVC/PCD from Ajtai commitments. Our approach is highly modular and generic. We begin by adapting the definition of customizable constraint systems [STW23a] to the ring setting.

<span id="page-39-3"></span>**Definition 4.1** (CCS over rings). Let pp :=  $(n_r, n_c, t, n_s, \deg, \ell_{in})$  be the integer public parameters<sup>2</sup> and let  $\bar{\mathcal{R}}$  be an arbitrary ring. Let  $\mathring{\mathbf{i}}$  be an index that consists of (i) t matrices  $M_1, \ldots, M_t \in \bar{\mathcal{R}}^{n_r \times n_c}$  with  $O(n_r + n_c)$  non-zero entries; (ii)  $n_s$  multisets  $S_1, \ldots, S_{n_s} \subseteq [t]$  such that  $|S_i| \leq \deg$  for all  $i \in [n_s]$ ; and (iii)  $n_s$  scalars  $c_1, \ldots, c_{n_s} \in \bar{\mathcal{R}}$ .

We denote by  $\operatorname{\mathsf{pp}}_{\mathsf{ccs}} := (\operatorname{\mathsf{pp}}, \mathbb{i})$  the index-specific parameters. Given a tuple  $(\operatorname{\mathsf{pp}}_{\mathsf{ccs}}, \mathbb{x} \in \bar{\mathcal{R}}^{\ell_{\mathsf{in}}}; \mathbb{w} \in \bar{\mathcal{R}}^{n_c-\ell_{\mathsf{in}}-1})$  and let  $\vec{\mathbf{z}} := (\mathbb{x}, 1, \mathbb{w}) \in \bar{\mathcal{R}}^{n_c}$ . We say  $(\operatorname{\mathsf{pp}}_{\mathsf{ccs}}, \mathbb{x}; \mathbb{w})$  is in the relation  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{ccs}}$  (over ring  $\bar{\mathcal{R}}$ ) if and only if

$$\sum_{i=1}^{n_s} c_i \cdot \bigcirc_{j \in S_i} (M_j \cdot \vec{\mathbf{z}}) = 0^{n_r}.$$

<span id="page-39-2"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>2</sup>Informally,  $n_r$  denotes the number of constraints,  $n_c$  denotes the extended witness size and deg is the custom gate degree.

Here  $\bigcirc$  denotes the Hadamard product between vectors. And 0 (and 1) is the additive (and multiplicative) identity in  $\bar{\mathcal{R}}$  respectively.

<span id="page-40-3"></span>**Remark 4.1** (Packing multiple CCS field constraints). If the ring  $\bar{\mathcal{R}}$  is isomorphic to  $\mathbb{F}^k$  for a field  $\mathbb{F}$ , we can pack k instance-witness pairs for the CCS relation over  $\mathbb{F}$  into a single instance-witness pair for the CCS relation over  $\bar{\mathcal{R}}$ . More precisely, a set of k tuples  $((\mathsf{pp},\mathring{\mathbb{I}}_i), \varkappa_i, \varkappa_i)_{i=1}^k$ , are all in the relation  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{ccs}}$  over  $\mathbb{F}$  if and only if the transformed tuple  $((\mathsf{pp},\mathring{\mathbb{I}}^*), \varkappa^*, \varkappa^*)$  is in the relation  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{ccs}}$  over  $\bar{\mathcal{R}}$ . Each entry  $\mathbf{e} \in \bar{\mathcal{R}}$  in  $(\mathring{\mathbb{I}}^*, \varkappa^*, \varkappa^*)$  is set such that  $\mathsf{NTT}(\mathbf{e}) = (e_1, \ldots, e_k)$ , where  $e_i \in \mathbb{F}$  is the corresponding entry in  $(\mathring{\mathbb{I}}_i, \varkappa_i, \varkappa_i)$  for  $1 \leq i \leq k$ .

#### <span id="page-40-0"></span>4.1 Lattice-based Committed CCS

Next, we introduce the lattice-based committed CCS relation  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{cmccs}}$  that extends the commitment opening relation  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{cm}}$  in Eq. (8) to the CCS setting. A folding scheme for  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{cmccs}}$  would allow us to build an IVC/PCD scheme.

Intuitively, a witness of the committed CCS relation consists of a pair  $(\vec{\mathbf{f}}, \vec{\mathbf{w}})$ , and the relation checks that (i)  $\vec{\mathbf{w}}$  is a valid witness for the CCS instance  $\mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}}$ , (ii)  $\vec{\mathbf{f}}$  is a low-norm opening of the Ajtai commitment cm, and (iii)  $\vec{\mathbf{f}}$  is the gadget decomposition of the witness  $\vec{\mathbf{w}}$ , meaning  $\vec{\mathbf{w}} = \mathbf{G} \times \vec{\mathbf{f}}$  for the gadget  $\mathbf{G}$ . We formally define the relation below.

<span id="page-40-2"></span>**Definition 4.2** (Lattice-based committed CCS relation). Let  $\mathcal{R}_q := \mathbb{Z}_q[X]/(X^d+1)$  where q is a prime and d is a power of two. Let  $\mathsf{pp} := (\mathsf{pp}_\mathsf{cm}, \mathsf{pp}_\mathsf{ccs})$  be the public parameters where  $\mathsf{pp}_\mathsf{cm} = (\kappa, m, B < q/2, \mathbf{A})$  is the public parameter for  $\mathcal{R}_\mathsf{cm}^B$  (Eq. (8)) and  $\mathsf{pp}_\mathsf{ccs} = (n_r, n_c, t, n_s, \deg, \ell_\mathsf{in}, \mathring{\mathfrak{h}})$  (defined in Definition 4.1) is for  $\mathcal{R}_\mathsf{ccs}$  (over  $\mathcal{R}_q$ ).

Set  $\ell := m/n_c \in \mathbb{N}$  such that  $B^{\ell} \geq q/2$ . Let  $\mathbf{G} := \mathbf{I}_{n_c} \otimes [1, B, \dots, B^{\ell-1}] \in \mathbb{Z}_q^{n_c \times m}$  be the gadget matrix. The indexed relation  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{cmccs}}^B$  is defined as

<span id="page-40-1"></span>
$$\mathcal{R}^{B}_{\mathsf{cmccs}} := \left\{ \begin{array}{l} \left( \mathsf{pp}, \mathbf{x} := (\mathsf{cm} \in \mathcal{R}^{\kappa}_{q}, \mathbf{x}_{\mathsf{ccs}} \in \mathcal{R}^{\ell_{\mathsf{in}}}_{q}); \mathbf{w} := (\vec{\mathbf{f}} \in \mathcal{R}^{m}_{q}, \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{ccs}} \in \mathcal{R}^{n-\ell_{\mathsf{in}}-1}_{q}) \right) s.t. \\ \left( \mathsf{pp}_{\mathsf{cm}}, \mathsf{cm}; \vec{\mathbf{f}} \right) \in \mathcal{R}^{B}_{\mathsf{cm}} \wedge \left( \mathsf{pp}_{\mathsf{ccs}}, \mathbf{x}_{\mathsf{ccs}}; \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{ccs}} \right) \in \mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{ccs}} \wedge \left( \mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}} = \mathbf{G} \times \vec{\mathbf{f}} \right) \end{array} \right\},$$

$$(33)$$

where  $\mathbf{z}_{\text{ccs}} := (\mathbf{z}_{\text{ccs}}, 1, \mathbf{w}_{\text{ccs}}) \in \mathcal{R}_q^{n_c}$ .

**Remark 4.2.** The constraint  $\mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}} = \mathbf{G} \times \mathbf{\vec{f}}$  is used to capture that  $\mathbf{\vec{f}}$  is the "base-B" representation of the original witness  $\mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}}$  in CCS. Crucially, consider a witness  $(\mathbf{\vec{f}}, \mathsf{w}_{\mathsf{ccs}})$  for instance  $(\mathsf{cm}, \mathsf{x}_{\mathsf{ccs}})$ . We know that  $\mathbf{\vec{f}}$  is a low-norm opening for the Ajtai binding commitment  $\mathsf{cm}$  given that  $(\mathsf{cm}, \mathbf{\vec{f}})$  is in  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{cm}}^B$ . This implies that  $\mathsf{w}_{\mathsf{ccs}}$  is also bound to  $\mathsf{cm}$  because the equation  $(\mathsf{x}_{\mathsf{ccs}}, 1, \mathsf{w}_{\mathsf{ccs}}) = \mathbf{G} \times \mathbf{\vec{f}}$  holds.

**Remark 4.3.** We set  $(\mathbb{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}}, 1, \mathbb{w}_{\mathsf{ccs}}) = \mathbf{G} \times \mathbf{\vec{f}}$  only for ease of exposition. Note that the integrity of  $\mathbb{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}}$  is already guaranteed by the verifier checks. Thus it suffices to decompose  $\mathbb{w}_{\mathsf{ccs}}$  to  $\mathbf{\vec{f}}$  and check the statement  $\mathbb{w}_{\mathsf{ccs}} = \mathbf{G} \times \mathbf{\vec{f}}$ .

The expanded relation. Similar to the paradigm in Section 3.1, to construct a folding scheme for  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{comp}} := \mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{cmccs}}$ , we introduce a new relation  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{acc}} := \mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{evalccs}}$  that augments  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{cmccs}}$  with a multilinear evaluation statement. Note that in  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{evalccs}}$ , we replace the high-degree custom gate relation  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{cmccs}}$  with a linearized relation  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{lccs}}$ . Like the linearization framework from Hypernova [KS23b], this adjustment is necessary because our folding scheme runs sum-checks to reduce the norm constraints and the high-degree custom gate constraints in  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{cmccs}}$  into linearized statements. Hence, we must modify the accumulated relation accordingly. Notably,  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{evalccs}}$  extends  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{eval}}$  from Eq. (9).

<span id="page-41-3"></span>**Definition 4.3** (Lattice-based linearized CCS relation). Let  $pp := (pp_{cm}, pp_{ccs})$  be the public parameters in Definition 4.2 where  $\ell := m/n_c \in \mathbb{N}$  and  $B^{\ell} \geq q/2$ . Without loss of generality<sup>3</sup>, we assume that the number of rows  $n_r$  in CCS matrices equals to the committed witness length m.

We define the linearized CCS relation  $\mathcal{R}_{lccs}$  as the set of tuples

$$(\mathsf{pp}_{\mathsf{ccs}}, \mathsf{x} \vcentcolon= (\vec{\mathbf{r}} \in \mathcal{R}_q^{\log m}, [\mathbf{u}_j]_{j=1}^t \in \mathcal{R}_q^t, \mathsf{x}_{\mathsf{ccs}} \in \mathcal{R}_q^{\ell_{\mathsf{in}}}, \mathbf{h} \in \mathcal{R}_q); \, \mathsf{w} \vcentcolon= \mathsf{w}_{\mathsf{ccs}} \in \mathcal{R}_q^{n_c - \ell_{\mathsf{in}} - 1})$$

such that for all  $j \in [t]$ :

<span id="page-41-4"></span>
$$\mathbf{u}_{j} = \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log n_{c}}} \mathsf{mle}\left[M_{j}\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \vec{\mathbf{b}}) \cdot \mathsf{mle}\left[\mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}}\right](\vec{\mathbf{b}}). \tag{34}$$

Here  $\operatorname{mle}[M_j] \in \mathcal{R}_q^{\leq 1}[X_1, \ldots, X_{\log n_r + \log n_c}]$  and  $\operatorname{mle}[\mathbf{z}_{\operatorname{ccs}}] \in \mathcal{R}_q^{\leq 1}[X_1, \ldots, X_{\log n_c}]$  are the multilinear extensions of matrix  $M_j \in \mathcal{R}_q^{n_r \times n_c}$  and  $\mathbf{z}_{\operatorname{ccs}} := (\mathsf{w}_{\operatorname{ccs}}, \mathbf{h}, \mathsf{x}_{\operatorname{ccs}}) \in \mathcal{R}_q^{n_c}$  respectively.  $\mathcal{R}_{\operatorname{evalccs}}^B$  is defined as

<span id="page-41-2"></span>
$$\mathcal{R}_{\text{evalccs}}^{B} := \left\{ \begin{array}{l} \left( \mathsf{pp}, \mathbf{x} := (\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \mathsf{cm}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}, [\mathbf{u}_{j}]_{j=1}^{t}, \mathbf{x}_{\mathsf{ccs}}, \mathbf{h}); \\ \mathbf{w} := (\vec{\mathbf{f}} \in \mathcal{R}_{q}^{m}, \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{ccs}}) \right) s.t. \\ \left( \mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}} = \mathbf{G}\vec{\mathbf{f}} \right) \wedge \left( \mathsf{pp}_{\mathsf{cm}}, (\mathsf{cm}, \vec{\mathbf{r}}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}); \vec{\mathbf{f}} \right) \in \mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{eval}}^{B} \\ \wedge \left( \mathsf{pp}_{\mathsf{ccs}}, (\vec{\mathbf{r}}, [\mathbf{u}_{j}]_{j=1}^{t}, \mathbf{x}_{\mathsf{ccs}}, \mathbf{h}); \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{ccs}} \right) \in \mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{lccs}} \end{array} \right\}, \tag{35}$$

where  $\mathbf{G} := \mathbf{I}_{n_c} \otimes [1, B, \dots, B^{\ell-1}] \in \mathbb{Z}_q^{n_c \times m}$  and  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{eval}}^B$  is defined in Eq. (9).

#### <span id="page-41-0"></span>4.2 A Generic Folding Scheme for CCS

In this section, we construct a folding scheme for  $\mathcal{R}_{acc} := \mathcal{R}^B_{evalccs}$  and  $\mathcal{R}_{comp} := \mathcal{R}^B_{cmccs}$ , or equivalently, a reduction of knowledge (Definition 2.5) from  $\mathcal{R}^B_{evalccs} \times \mathcal{R}^B_{cmccs}$  to  $\mathcal{R}^B_{evalccs}$ . The scheme is presented for modularity and illustration purposes. In Section 4.3, we introduce an optimized version with better efficiency.

Similar to the strategy in Section 3.2, the construction consists of three steps.

<span id="page-41-1"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>3</sup>We can always pad dummy constraints/witnesses to enforce  $n_r = m$ .

- Step 1: Linearization. First, we reduce the relation  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\text{evalccs}} \times \mathcal{R}^B_{\text{cmccs}}$  to  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\text{evalccs}} \times \mathcal{R}^B_{\text{evalccs}} \times \mathcal{R}^B_{\text{evalccs}}$  via a protocol  $\Pi_{\text{ccs}}$  (Figure 5) that reduces  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\text{cmccs}}$  to  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\text{evalccs}}$ . The protocol  $\Pi_{\text{ccs}}$  runs a sum-check to reduce the high-degree custom gates check to a degree-1 check (e.g., a multilinear evaluation check). Similar to the expansion step in Section 3.2, the linearization step reduces to a linear relation with evaluation-like statements.
- Step 2: Decomposition. Next, using a protocol  $\Pi_{\text{ccsdec}}$  (Figure 6), we reduce the relation  $\mathcal{R}_{\text{evalccs}}^B \times \mathcal{R}_{\text{evalccs}}^B$  to a relation

$$(\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{evalccs}}^b)^{2k} := \underbrace{\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{evalccs}}^b \times \cdots \times \mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{evalccs}}^b}_{2k}$$

where b, k are chosen such that  $b^k = B$ . We note that  $\Pi_{\mathsf{ccsdec}}$  is an adaptation to  $\Pi_{\mathsf{dec}}$  (Figure 2) with similar analysis.

Step 3: Folding. Finally, we reduce  $(\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{evalccs}}^b)^{2k}$  back to  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{evalccs}}^B$  using a protocol  $\Pi_{\mathsf{ccsfold}}$  (Figure 7). Note that  $\Pi_{\mathsf{ccsfold}}$  is an adaptation to  $\Pi_{\mathsf{fold}}$  (Figure 3) with similar analysis.

By the composition theorems for reductions of knowledge (Theorem 2.1, Theorem 2.2), the composed protocol  $\Pi_{\text{mccsfold}} := \Pi_{\text{ccsfold}} \circ \Pi_{\text{ccsdec}} \circ \Pi_{\text{ccs}}$  is a reduction of knowledge from  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\text{evalccs}} \times \mathcal{R}^B_{\text{evalccs}}$  to  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\text{evalccs}}$  as desired. We formally state the result in Theorem 4.1.

<span id="page-42-1"></span>**Theorem 4.1.** Let  $\mathcal{R}_q \cong \mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}^{d/\tau}$  for some  $\tau \in \mathbb{N}$  where  $\tau \mid d$  and  $1/q^{\tau}$  is in  $\operatorname{negl}(\lambda)$ . Let  $\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}} \subseteq \mathcal{R}_q$  be a strong sampling set for which  $1/|\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}|$  is in  $\operatorname{negl}(\lambda)$ , and the expansion factor  $T := \|\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{small}}\|_{\mathsf{op}} \leq c$  (Definition 6) for some  $c \in \mathbb{N}$ . Let  $\mathcal{C}$  be the strong sampling set as in Eq. (31). Let  $\mathsf{pp}_{\mathsf{cm}} := (\kappa, m, \mathbf{A}, B < q/2)$  and  $\mathsf{pp}_{\mathsf{ccs}} := (n_r := m, n_c, t, n_s, \deg, \ell_{\mathsf{in}}, [M_j]_{j=1}^t, [S_i, c_i]_{i=1}^{n_s})$  be the public parameters such that  $B^{m/n_c} \geq q/2$  and  $\mathsf{MSIS}_{\kappa,m,8TB}^{\infty,q}$  is hard. Set b, k such that 2kc(b-1) < B and  $b^k = B$ . Let  $\Pi_{\mathsf{ccs}}$ ,  $\Pi_{\mathsf{ccsdec}}$ ,  $\Pi_{\mathsf{ccsfold}}$  be the protocols in Figure 5, Figure 6 and Figure 7, respectively. The composed protocol  $\Pi_{\mathsf{mccsfold}} := \Pi_{\mathsf{ccsfold}} \circ \Pi_{\mathsf{ccsdec}} \circ \Pi_{\mathsf{ccs}}$  is a public-coin reduction of knowledge from relation  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{evalccs}}^B \times \mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{cmccs}}^B$  to  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{evalccs}}^B$ .

*Proof.* The protocol is public-coin as the three subprotocols are all public-coin. For the case where  $\mathcal{R}_q \cong \mathbb{Z}_q^d$ , the Theorem follows from Lemma 4.1, Lemma 4.2, Theorem 4.2 and the knowledge composition theorems (Theorem 2.1 and Theorem 2.2). For the case where  $\mathcal{R}_q \cong \mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}^{d/\tau}$ , the same optimization in Section 3.3 can be used to extend Theorem 4.1 to support small modulus q.

# <span id="page-42-0"></span>4.2.1 Linearization: The reduction from $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{cmccs}}^B$ to $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{evalccs}}^B$

By Theorem 2.2, to reduce from  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\text{evalccs}} \times \mathcal{R}^B_{\text{emccs}}$  to  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\text{evalccs}} \times \mathcal{R}^B_{\text{evalccs}}$ , it suffices to construct a protocol that reduces  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\text{cmccs}}$  (Eq. (33)) to  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\text{evalccs}}$  (Eq. (35)). We describe the

**Parameters:** A strong sampling set  $\mathcal{C} := \mathbb{Z}_q \subseteq \mathcal{R}_q$  (Definition 2.1)

 $\textbf{Input:} \ \mathtt{x} \coloneqq (\mathsf{cm}, \mathtt{x}_\mathsf{ccs}) \in \mathcal{R}^\kappa_q \times \mathcal{R}^{\ell_\mathsf{in}}_q \ \text{and} \ \mathtt{w} \coloneqq (\vec{\mathbf{f}}, \mathtt{w}_\mathsf{ccs}) \in \mathcal{R}^m_q \times \mathcal{R}^{n_c - \ell_\mathsf{in} - 1}_q$ 

**Output:**  $\mathbb{x}_o := (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o \in \mathcal{R}_q^{\log m}, \hat{\mathbf{v}} \in \mathcal{R}_q, \mathsf{cm}, [\mathbf{u}_j \in \mathcal{R}_q]_{j=1}^t, \mathbb{x}_{\mathsf{ccs}}, 1) \text{ and } \mathbb{w}_o := (\vec{\mathbf{f}}, \mathbb{w}_{\mathsf{ccs}})$ 

The protocol  $\langle P(pp, x; w), V(pp, x) \rangle$ :

- 1.  $V \to P$ : V sends P a random vector  $\vec{\beta} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{C}^{\log m}$ .
- 2.  $P \leftrightarrow V$ : Let  $\mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}} := (\mathbb{x}_{\mathsf{ccs}}, 1, \mathbb{w}_{\mathsf{ccs}})$  and let  $\mathsf{deg}$  denote the CCS gate degree, define the polynomial  $g \in \mathcal{R}_q^{\leq \mathsf{deg}+1}[X_1, \dots, X_{\log m}]$

$$g(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) := eq(\vec{\beta}, \vec{\mathbf{x}}) \cdot \left( \sum_{i=1}^{n_s} c_i \cdot \left[ \prod_{j \in S_i} \left( \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log n_c}} \mathsf{mle}\left[M_j\right](\vec{\mathbf{x}}, \vec{\mathbf{b}}) \cdot \mathsf{mle}\left[\mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}}\right](\vec{\mathbf{b}}) \right) \right] \right)$$

P and V run a sum-check protocol for the claim  $\sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}} g(\vec{\mathbf{b}}) = 0$ .

Let  $\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{C}^{\log m}$  be the sum-check challenge vector. The protocol reduces to a random evaluation check  $g(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o) \stackrel{?}{=} s$  for some  $s \in \mathcal{R}_q$ .

3.  $P \to V$ : P sends V the values  $(\hat{\mathbf{v}}, [\mathbf{u}_j]_{j=1}^t)$  where  $\hat{\mathbf{v}} := \mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o)$  and for every  $j \in [t]$ ,  $\mathbf{u}_j$  is computed as

$$\mathbf{u}_{j} := \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log n_{c}}} \mathsf{mle}\left[M_{j}\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_{o}, \vec{\mathbf{b}}) \cdot \mathsf{mle}\left[\mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}}\right](\vec{\mathbf{b}}) \,.$$

<span id="page-43-1"></span>4. V computes  $\mathbf{e} := eq(\vec{\beta}, \vec{\mathbf{r}}_o)$  and checks that

$$\mathbf{e} \cdot \left( \sum_{i=1}^{n_s} c_i \cdot \prod_{j \in S_i} \mathbf{u}_j \right) \stackrel{?}{=} s.$$

5. V outputs  $\mathbf{z}_o := (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o, \hat{\mathbf{v}}, \mathsf{cm}, [\mathbf{u}_j]_{j=1}^t, \mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}}, 1)$ . P outputs  $\mathbf{w}_o := (\vec{\mathbf{f}}, \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{ccs}})$ .

<span id="page-43-0"></span>Figure 5: The protocol  $\Pi_{ccs}$  that reduces  $\mathcal{R}^B_{cmccs}$  to  $\mathcal{R}^B_{evalccs}$ .

protocol  $\Pi_{ccs}$  in Figure 5. The protocol is inspired by the linearization technique from Hypernova [KS23b]. Intuitively, it runs a sum-check to reduce the high-degree CCS relation to a multilinear evaluation relation that has degree 1.
