# <span id="page-65-0"></span>A Multilinear Evaluation Mapping Lemma

We derive a lemma from the fact that every ring homomorphism  $\phi: R \to S$  induces a natural homomorphism  $\phi': R[X] \to S[X]$  over the polynomial rings. In the special case where  $\mathcal{R}_q \cong \mathbb{Z}_q^d$ , consider a vector  $\vec{\mathbf{f}} \in \mathcal{R}_q^m$  and a vector  $\hat{\mathbf{f}} \in \mathcal{R}_q^m$  such that  $\mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{f}}) = \mathsf{Coef}(\vec{\mathbf{f}})$ . Let  $f_1, \ldots, f_d$  be the multilinear extensions of the columns of  $\mathsf{Coef}(\vec{\mathbf{f}}) \in \mathbb{Z}_q^{m \times d}$ . The lemma asserts that a multilinear evaluation of  $\mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}\right]$  can be mapped to the evaluations of  $f_1, \ldots, f_d$  (over  $\mathbb{Z}_q$ ) through the NTT isomorphism. This lemma helps maintain the invariant of the evaluation statement  $\hat{\mathbf{v}} = \mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}})$  after folding the witness  $\vec{\mathbf{f}}$ , even if the evaluation point  $\vec{\mathbf{r}} \in \mathcal{R}_q^{\log m}$  changes after the folding.

<span id="page-65-4"></span>**Lemma A.1.** Let  $\mathcal{R}_q \cong \mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}^{d/\tau}$  for some  $\tau \in \mathbb{N}$  where  $\tau \mid d$ . Let  $m \in \mathbb{N}$  be a power of two. For any  $\vec{\mathbf{f}} \in \mathcal{R}_q^m$ , let  $\hat{\mathbf{f}} := (\hat{\mathbf{f}}_1, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{f}}_{\tau}) \in \mathcal{R}_q^{m \times \tau}$  denote the vector such that  $\mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{f}}) = \mathsf{Coef}(\vec{\mathbf{f}}) \in \mathbb{Z}_q^{m \times d}$ . Let  $\vec{\mathbf{r}} \in \mathcal{R}_q^{\log m}$  and denote  $(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_1^*, \dots, \vec{\mathbf{r}}_{d/\tau}^*) \in (\mathbb{F}_{q^{\tau}}^{\log m})^{d/\tau}$  the columns of

 $\mathsf{NTT}(\vec{\mathbf{r}})$ . For every  $i \in [\tau]$ , we have that  $\mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}) \in \mathcal{R}_q$  is mapped to

$$\left(\mathsf{mle}\left[\mathsf{Coef}_{1+(i-1)\cdot d/\tau}(\vec{\mathbf{f}})\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_1^*),\dots,\mathsf{mle}\left[\mathsf{Coef}_{i\cdot d/\tau}(\vec{\mathbf{f}})\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_{d/\tau}^*)\right)\in\mathbb{F}_{q^\tau}^{d/\tau}$$

by the NTT isomorphism. Recall that  $\mathsf{mle}\left[\cdot\right]$  denotes multilinear extensions (Definition 2.4) and  $\mathsf{Coef}_j(\vec{\mathbf{f}}) \in \mathbb{Z}_q^m$  is the jth  $(1 \leq j \leq d)$  column of  $\mathsf{Coef}(\vec{\mathbf{f}})$ .

*Proof.* By definition of  $\hat{\mathbf{f}}$ , we have that

$$\mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{f}}) = \left[\mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{f}}_1), \dots, \mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{f}}_{\tau})\right] = \left[\mathsf{Coef}_1(\vec{\mathbf{f}}), \dots, \mathsf{Coef}_d(\vec{\mathbf{f}})\right]. \tag{42}$$

Also observe that

$$\left(\mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_{1}\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}), \dots, \mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_{\tau}\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}})\right) = \left(\left\langle \hat{\mathbf{f}}_{j}, \bigotimes_{i=1}^{\log m} (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_{i}, 1 - \vec{\mathbf{r}}_{i})\right\rangle\right)_{i=1}^{\tau}$$
(43)

where  $\bigotimes$  denotes tensor product over  $\mathcal{R}_q$ . By the Chinese Remainder Theorem, the NTT map is an isomorphism, and the lemma follows from the properties of an isomorphism.

## <span id="page-66-0"></span>B Deferred Proofs

#### <span id="page-66-1"></span>B.1 Proof of Lemma 4.1

*Proof.* Public reducibility: Given input instance  $\mathbf{z} = (\mathsf{cm}, \mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}})$  and transcript that includes  $(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o, \hat{\mathbf{v}}, [\mathbf{u}_j]_{j=1}^t)$ , the algorithm f outputs  $\mathbf{z}_o = (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o, \hat{\mathbf{v}}, \mathsf{cm}, [\mathbf{u}_j]_{j=1}^t, \mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}}, 1)$  if the verifier check passes; and  $\perp$  otherwise.

<u>Completeness:</u> Let  $(x; w) := ((cm, x_{ccs}); (\vec{f}, w_{ccs})) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(pp)$  denotes adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ 's output for  $\mathcal{R}_1 := \mathcal{R}^B_{cmccs}$ , where  $pp \leftarrow Setup(1^{\lambda})$  is the public parameter. WLOG, we assume that  $(pp, x; w) \in \mathcal{R}^B_{cmccs}$  (where  $\mathcal{R}^B_{cmccs}$  is specified in Definition 4.2). The protocol  $\langle P(pp, x, w), V(pp, x) \rangle$  proceeds as follows:

- 1. After running the sum-check and receiving the challenge vector  $\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o \in \mathcal{C}^{\log m}$ , P sends V the value  $\hat{\mathbf{v}} := \mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o)$ . Moreover, let  $\mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}} := (\mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}}, 1, \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{ccs}})$ , for every  $j \in [t]$ , P sends  $\mathbf{u}_j := \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log n_c}} \mathsf{mle}\left[M_j\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o, \vec{\mathbf{b}}) \cdot \mathsf{mle}\left[\mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}}\right](\vec{\mathbf{b}})$ .
- 2. V outputs  $\perp$  and halts if the check at Step 4 fails.
- 3. P outputs  $w_o := w = (\vec{\mathbf{f}}, w_{\mathsf{ccs}})$ . V outputs  $z_o := (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o, \hat{\mathbf{v}}, \mathsf{cm}, [\mathbf{u}_j]_{j=1}^t, z_{\mathsf{ccs}}, 1)$ .

First, by definitions of  $[\mathbf{u}_j]_{j=1}^t$ , we have that V passes the check at Step 4 and accepts.

Next we argue that the protocol's output  $(pp, \aleph_o; \aleph_o)$  is in the relation  $\mathcal{R}_2 := \mathcal{R}^B_{\text{evalccs}}$  (Eq. (35)) and completeness holds. It suffices to check that  $\mathbf{z}_{\text{ccs}} = \mathbf{G}\mathbf{f}$  and certain statements are in  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\text{eval}}$  and  $\mathcal{R}_{\text{lccs}}$  respectively. We argue them one by one:

- 1.  $\mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}} = \mathbf{G}\vec{\mathbf{f}}$  because  $(\mathsf{pp}, \mathsf{x}; \mathsf{w}) \in \mathcal{R}^{B}_{\mathsf{cmccs}}$  by assumption.
- 2.  $(\mathsf{pp}, (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o, \hat{\mathbf{v}}, \mathsf{cm}); \vec{\mathbf{f}})$  is in  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{eval}}^B$  because (i)  $\hat{\mathbf{v}} = \mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o)$  and (ii)  $(\mathsf{pp}, \mathsf{cm}, \vec{\mathbf{f}})$  is in  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{cm}}^B$  by the assumption that  $(\mathsf{pp}, \mathsf{x}; \mathsf{w})$  is in  $\mathcal{R}_1 := \mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{cmccs}}^B$ .
- by the assumption that (pp, x; w) is in  $\mathcal{R}_1 := \mathcal{R}_{cmccs}^{B^L}$ . 3.  $(pp_{ccs}, (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o, [\mathbf{u}_j]_{j=1}^t, x_{ccs}, \mathbf{h}); w_{ccs})$  is in  $\mathcal{R}_{lccs}$  by the assignments of  $[\mathbf{u}_j]_{j=1}^t$ .

<u>Knowledge soundness:</u> Let  $(z := (cm, z_{ccs}), state) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(pp)$  denote adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ 's chosen input for  $\mathcal{R}_1 := \mathcal{R}^B_{cmccs}$ , where  $pp \leftarrow \mathsf{Setup}(1^{\lambda})$  is the public parameter. The extractor Ext proceeds as follows:

- 1. Simulate the protocol  $\langle P^*(pp, x, state), V(pp, x) \rangle$  where  $P^*$  is the malicious prover.
- 2. Abort and output  $\perp$  if V rejects.
- 3. Otherwise, let  $(\mathbf{z}_o, \mathbf{w}_o)$  be the protocol output where  $\mathbf{z}_o := (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o, \hat{\mathbf{v}}, \mathsf{cm}, [\mathbf{u}_j]_{j=1}^t, \mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}}, 1)$  and  $\mathbf{w}_o := (\vec{\mathbf{f}}, \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{ccs}})$ . Abort and output  $\bot$  if  $(\mathsf{pp}, \mathbf{z}_o, \mathbf{w}_o) \notin \mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{evalccs}}$  (Eq. (35)).
- 4. Otherwise, if  $(pp, x_o, w_o) \in \mathcal{R}^B_{\text{evalors}}$ , the extractor outputs  $w := (\vec{\mathbf{f}}, w_{\text{ccs}})$ .

Let  $E_{\mathsf{bad}}$  denote the bad event that (i) V accepts and the protocol's output  $(\mathsf{x}_o, \mathsf{w}_o)$  satisfies that  $(\mathsf{pp}, \mathsf{x}_o, \mathsf{w}_o) \in \mathcal{R}_2 := \mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{evalccs}}$  but (ii)  $(\mathsf{pp}, \mathsf{x}; \mathsf{w})$  is not in  $\mathcal{R}_1 := \mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{cmccs}}$  (Eq. (33)). To prove knowledge soundness, it suffices to argue that  $\Pr[E_{\mathsf{bad}}] \leq \frac{(2b+1)\log m}{|\mathcal{C}|}$ .

Note that if  $(pp, \mathbb{x}_o, \mathbb{w}_o)$  is in  $\mathcal{R}_2 := \mathcal{R}^B_{\text{evalccs}}$  (Eq. (35)), the following hold: (i)  $(\mathbf{z}_{\text{ccs}} = \mathbf{G}\vec{\mathbf{f}})$ , (ii)  $(pp, \mathsf{cm}; \vec{\mathbf{f}})$  is in  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\text{cm}}$ , and (iii)  $(pp_{\mathsf{ccs}}, (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o, [\mathbf{u}]^t_{i=1}, \mathbb{x}_{\mathsf{ccs}}, 1); \mathbb{w}_{\mathsf{ccs}})$  is in  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{lccs}}$  (Eq. (34)). From (i) and (ii), the sumcheck polynomial g is fixed before sampling  $\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o$ , as the witness  $\mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}}$  is bound to  $\mathsf{cm}$ . Additionally, from (iii) and because the verifier check at Step 4 passes, the sum-check random evaluation  $g(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o) \stackrel{?}{=} s$  passes. Therefore, if  $\sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}} g(\vec{\mathbf{b}}) \neq 0$ , by sumcheck soundness, the probability that  $(pp, \mathbb{x}_o, \mathbb{w}_o) \in \mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{evalccs}}$  is at most  $\frac{2b \log m}{|\mathcal{C}|}$  (over the sum-check challenges).

Next we argue that if  $(pp_{ccs}, \mathbb{X}_{ccs}; \mathbb{W}_{ccs}) \notin \mathcal{R}_{ccs}$ , then  $\sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}} g(\vec{\mathbf{b}}) \neq 0$  with high probability. Define multilinear polynomial  $p(\vec{\mathbf{x}})$  as

$$p(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) := \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}} eq(\vec{\mathbf{x}}, \vec{\mathbf{b}}) \cdot \left( \sum_{i=1}^{n_s} c_i \cdot \prod_{j \in S_i} \left( \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{y}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log n_c}} \mathsf{mle}\left[M_j\right](\vec{\mathbf{b}}, \vec{\mathbf{y}}) \cdot \mathsf{mle}\left[\mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}}\right](\vec{\mathbf{y}}) \right) \right) \,.$$

By definition of g, it's clear that  $\sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}} g(\vec{\mathbf{b}}) = 0$  if and only if  $p(\vec{\beta}) = 0$ . Moreover,  $(pp_{ccs}, \aleph_{ccs}; \aleph_{ccs}) \notin \mathcal{R}_{ccs}$  (Definition 4.1) implies that  $p(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) \neq 0$  for some  $\vec{\mathbf{x}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}$  and

 $p(\vec{\mathbf{x}})$  is not a zero polynomial. Since  $\vec{\beta} \stackrel{\hspace{0.1em}\mathsf{\scriptscriptstyle\$}}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{C}^{\log m}$  is uniformly chosen from the sampling set  $\mathcal{C}$  (Defn 2.1), by the Generalized Schwartz-Zippel Lemma (Lemma 2.4), the probability that  $p(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) \neq 0$  while  $p(\vec{\beta}) = 0$  is at most  $\log m/|\mathcal{C}|$ .

In summary, the probability that  $E_{\mathsf{bad}}$  occurs is at most  $\frac{\log m}{|\mathcal{C}|} + \frac{2b \log m}{|\mathcal{C}|}$ , which finishes the proof.

#### <span id="page-68-0"></span>B.2 Proof of Lemma 4.2

Proof. Public reducibility: Given instance  $\mathbf{x} = (\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}, y, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{x}_w)$  and transcript  $[\hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, y_i, \mathbf{u}_i, \mathbf{x}_{w,i}]_{i=0}^{k-1}$ , one outputs  $[\mathbf{x}_i := (\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, y_i, \mathbf{u}_i, \mathbf{x}_{w,i})]_{i=0}^{k-1}$  if the verifier checks pass; otherwise it outputs  $\bot$ .

Completeness: Let  $(\mathbf{x}, \mathbf{w}) := ((\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}, y, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{x}_w), (\vec{\mathbf{f}}, \vec{\mathbf{w}})) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(\mathsf{pp})$  denote adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ 's chosen instance-witness pair for  $\mathcal{R}_1 := \mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{ccshom}}$  (Eq. (36)), where  $\mathsf{pp} := (\mathcal{L}, \mathcal{L}_w, \overline{M}) \leftarrow \mathsf{Setup}(1^\lambda)$  is the public parameter. WLOG we assume that  $(\mathsf{pp}, \mathbf{x}; \mathbf{w})$  is in  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{ccshom}}$ . The protocol  $\langle \mathsf{P}(\mathsf{pp}, \mathbf{x}, \mathbf{w}), \mathsf{V}(\mathsf{pp}, \mathbf{x}) \rangle$  proceeds as follows:

1. P computes  $\vec{\mathbf{F}} := (\vec{\mathbf{f}}_0, \dots, \vec{\mathbf{f}}_{k-1}) := \mathsf{split}_{b,k}(\vec{\mathbf{f}}) \; (\text{Eq. } (\frac{11}{2})) \text{ and sends V values}$ 

$$\begin{split} y_i &:= \mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i) \,, & \qquad \qquad \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i := \mathsf{mle} \left[ \hat{\mathbf{f}}_i \right] (\vec{\mathbf{r}}) \,, \\ \mathbf{u}_i &:= \left\langle \overline{M} \times \mathsf{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}), \mathcal{L}_w(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i) \right\rangle \,, & \qquad (\mathbf{z}_{w,i} || \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i) := \mathcal{L}_w(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i) \,. \end{split}$$

for every  $i \in [0, k)$ .

- 2. V outputs  $\perp$  and halts if the check  $\sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot [y_i, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, \mathbf{u}_i, \mathbf{x}_{w,i}] \stackrel{?}{=} [y, \hat{\mathbf{v}}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{x}_w]$  fails.
- 3. Poutputs  $[\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i, \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i]_{i=0}^{k-1}$ . Voutputs  $[\mathbf{z}_i := (\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, y_i, \mathbf{u}_i, \mathbf{z}_{w,i})]_{i=0}^{k-1}$ .

We first show that if V accepts, then the protocol's output satisfies that for all  $i \in [0, k)$ ,

$$(\mathsf{pp}, (\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, y_i, \mathbf{u}_i, \mathbf{x}_{w,i}); (\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i, \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i)) \in \mathcal{R}^b_{\mathsf{ccshom}}$$
.

This follows given how  $[y_i, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, \mathbf{u}_i, \mathbf{z}_{w,i}]_{i=0}^{k-1}$  are computed, and because  $\|\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i\|_{\infty} < b$  for all  $i \in [0, k)$  by the property of the algorithm  $\mathsf{split}_{b,k}(\vec{\mathbf{f}})$ .

It remains to argue that V will accept, that is, the check  $\sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot [y_i, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, \mathbf{u}_i, \mathbf{z}_{w,i}] \stackrel{?}{=} [y, \hat{\mathbf{v}}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{z}_w]$  passes. By Lemma 3.4, we have that

$$\sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot y_i = y, \qquad \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i = \hat{\mathbf{v}}.$$

Since  $\mathcal{L}_w$  is an  $\mathcal{R}_q$ -module homomorphism, by the same argument for proving  $\sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot y_i = y$ , it also holds that  $\sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \mathbf{z}_{w,i} = \mathbf{z}_w$ . Finally, we have that

$$\begin{split} \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \mathbf{u}_i &= \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \left\langle \overline{M} \times \mathsf{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}), \mathcal{L}_w(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i) \right\rangle = \left\langle \overline{M} \times \mathsf{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}), \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \mathcal{L}_w(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i) \right\rangle \\ &= \left\langle \overline{M} \times \mathsf{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}), \mathcal{L}_w \left( \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i \right) \right\rangle = \left\langle \overline{M} \times \mathsf{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}), \mathcal{L}_w(\vec{\mathbf{f}}) \right\rangle = \mathbf{u} \,. \end{split}$$

The 1st equality is by definition of  $[\mathbf{u}_i]_{i=0}^{k-1}$ ; the 2nd equality is by the property of inner products; the 3rd equality holds because  $\mathcal{L}_w$  is an  $\mathcal{R}_q$ -module homomorphism; the 4th equality is by definition of decomposition (Eq. (11)); the last equality holds because  $(\mathsf{pp}, \varkappa; \mathsf{w})$  is in  $\mathcal{R}_1 := \mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{ccshom}}$  (Eq. (36)) by assumption, whereas  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{ccshom}}$  checks that  $\langle \overline{M} \times \mathsf{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}), \mathcal{L}_w(\vec{\mathbf{f}}) \rangle = \mathbf{u}$ . Therefore, V will accept and thus completeness holds.

<u>Knowledge soundness:</u> Let  $(\mathbf{x} := (\hat{\mathbf{v}}, y, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{x}_w), \mathsf{state}) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(\mathsf{pp})$  denote adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ 's chosen input instance for  $\mathcal{R}_1 := \mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{ccshom}}$ , where  $\mathsf{pp} := (\mathcal{L}, \mathcal{L}_w, \overline{M}) \leftarrow \mathsf{Setup}(1^{\lambda})$  is the public parameter. The extractor Ext proceeds as follows:

- 1. Simulate the protocol  $\langle P^*(pp, x, state), V(pp, x) \rangle$  where  $P^*$  is the malicious prover.
- 2. Output  $\perp$  if  $\mathsf{V}$  rejects. Otherwise let  $(\mathsf{x}_o, \mathsf{w}_o) := [(\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, y_i, \mathbf{u}_i, \mathsf{x}_{w,i}); (\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i, \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i)]_{i=0}^{k-1}$  be the protocol output (note that  $\vec{\mathbf{r}}$  is the same as that in the input instance  $\mathsf{x}$  to pass the verification check). The extractor outputs witness  $\mathsf{w} := (\vec{\mathbf{f}}, \vec{\mathbf{w}})$  where

<span id="page-69-1"></span>
$$\vec{\mathbf{f}} := \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i, \qquad \vec{\mathbf{w}} := \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \mathcal{L}_w(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i)[n_{\mathsf{in}} + 1, n_{\mathsf{in}} + n]. \tag{44}$$

To prove knowledge soundness, it suffices to show that if V accepts and the output  $(\mathbb{z}_o, \mathbb{w}_o)$  satisfies that  $(\mathsf{pp}, \mathbb{z}_o, \mathbb{w}_o) \in \mathcal{R}_2 := (\mathcal{R}^b_{\mathsf{ccshom}})^k$ , then the extracted witness  $\mathbb{w}$  satisfies that  $(\mathsf{pp}, \mathbb{z}, \mathbb{w}) \in \mathcal{R}_1 := \mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{ccshom}}$ .

By Lemma 3.5, we have that  $(\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}, y; \vec{\mathbf{f}}) \in \mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{hom}}$  if  $[(\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, y_i); \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=0}^{k-1}$  is in  $(\mathcal{R}^b_{\mathsf{hom}})^k$ . By definition of  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{ccshom}}$  (Eq. (36)), it remains to argue that

<span id="page-69-0"></span>
$$\mathbf{z}_{i} := (\mathbf{z}_{w,i} || \vec{\mathbf{w}}_{i}) = \mathcal{L}_{w}(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_{i}) \,\forall i \in [0, k) \implies \mathbf{z} := (\mathbf{z}_{w} || \vec{\mathbf{w}}) = \mathcal{L}_{w}(\vec{\mathbf{f}}); \tag{45}$$

<span id="page-69-2"></span>
$$\mathbf{u}_i = \langle \overline{M} \times \mathsf{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}), \mathbf{z}_i \rangle \ \forall i \in [0, k) \implies \mathbf{u} = \langle \overline{M} \times \mathsf{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}), \mathbf{z} \rangle \ .$$
 (46)

We first prove Eq. (45). By the verifier check  $\sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \mathbf{z}_{w,i} = \mathbf{z}_w$  and by Eq. (44), we have that  $\mathbf{z} = \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \mathbf{z}_i$ . Since  $\mathcal{L}_w$  is an  $\mathcal{R}_q$ -module homomorphism, Eq. (45) holds by the same argument as in Lemma 3.2 for proving  $y = \mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{f}})$  (where we replace  $y, \mathcal{L}$  with  $\mathbf{z}, \mathcal{L}_w$  respectively).

Similarly, Eq. (46) holds because

$$\mathbf{u} = \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \mathbf{u}_i = \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \left\langle \overline{M} \times \mathsf{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}), \mathbf{z}_i \right\rangle = \left\langle \overline{M} \times \mathsf{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}), \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \mathbf{z}_i \right\rangle = \left\langle \overline{M} \times \mathsf{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}), \mathbf{z} \right\rangle$$

where the 1st equality is by the verifier check; the 2nd equality follows from the premise in Eq. (46); the 3rd equality follows from the linearly homomorphic property of inner products; the last equality holds as we've proved previously that  $\mathbf{z} = \sum_{i=0}^{k-1} b^i \cdot \mathbf{z}_i$ .

In summary,  $(\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}, y; \vec{\mathbf{f}})$  is in  $\mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{hom}}$  and Eq. (45), Eq. (46) hold true. Therefore, conditioned on that  $(\mathsf{pp}, [(\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, y_i, \mathbf{u}_i, \mathbf{z}_{w,i}); (\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i, \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i)]_{i=0}^k)$  is in  $\mathcal{R}_2 := (\mathcal{R}^b_{\mathsf{ccshom}})^k$ , the extracted witness  $(\vec{\mathbf{f}}, \vec{\mathbf{w}})$  will satisfy that  $(\mathsf{pp}, (\vec{\mathbf{r}}, \hat{\mathbf{v}}, y, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{z}_w); (\vec{\mathbf{f}}, \vec{\mathbf{w}}))$  is in  $\mathcal{R}_1 := \mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{ccshom}}$ , which completes the proof.

#### <span id="page-70-0"></span>B.3 Proof of Theorem 4.2

*Proof.* <u>Public reducibility:</u> Given input instances  $[\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, y_i, \mathbf{u}_i, \mathbf{z}_{w,i}]_{i=1}^{2k}$  and the transcript that includes challenges  $\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o$ , evaluations  $[\theta_i]_{i=1}^{2k}$ , values  $[\eta_i]_{i=1}^{2k}$ , and folding challenges  $[\rho_i]_{i=1}^{2k}$ . The algorithm f outputs  $\mathbf{z}_o := (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_o, y_o, \mathbf{u}_o, \mathbf{z}_{w,o})$  such that

$$\mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{v}}_o) = \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \mathsf{RotSum}(\rho_i, \mathsf{NTT}(\theta_i)) \,, \quad [y_o, \mathbf{u}_o, \mathbf{x}_{w,o}] := \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \rho_i \cdot [y_i, \eta_i, \mathbf{x}_{w,i}]$$

if the verifier checks pass; and output  $\bot$  otherwise. (RotSum defined in Lemma 2.1.) Completeness: Let

$$(\mathbf{x}, \mathbf{w}) := [\mathbf{x}_i = (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i, y_i, \mathbf{u}_i, \mathbf{x}_{w,i}), \mathbf{w}_i = (\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i, \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i)]_{i=1}^{2k} \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(\mathsf{pp})$$

denote adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ 's chosen instance-witness pair for  $\mathcal{R}_1 := (\mathcal{R}^b_{\mathsf{hom}})^{2k}$ , where  $\mathsf{pp} := (\mathcal{L}, \mathcal{L}_w, \overline{M} = M_1) \leftarrow \mathsf{Setup}(1^\lambda)$  is the public parameter. WLOG we assume that  $(\mathsf{pp}, \varkappa, w)$  is in  $\mathcal{R}_1 := (\mathcal{R}^b_{\mathsf{ccshom}})^{2k}$ . The protocol  $\langle \mathsf{P}(\mathsf{pp}, \varkappa, w), \mathsf{V}(\mathsf{pp}, \varkappa) \rangle$  proceeds as follows:

1. P and V honestly run the sum-check and P sends values  $[\theta_i, \eta_i]_{i=1}^{2k}$  honestly such that for every  $i \in [2k]$ ,

<span id="page-70-1"></span>
$$\eta_i := \left\langle \overline{M} \times \operatorname{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o), (\mathbf{z}_{w,i} || \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i) \right\rangle, \qquad \theta_i := \operatorname{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right] (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o).$$
(47)

Here tensor(·) is defined in Eq. (37) and  $\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o$  is the sum-check challenge vector.

2. V outputs  $\perp$  and halts if the check at Step 4 fails.

3. Otherwise, let  $[\rho_i]_{i=1}^{2k}$  be verifier's last folding challenges. Set  $(\hat{\mathbf{v}}_o, y_o, \mathbf{u}_o, \mathbf{z}_{w,o}, \vec{\mathbf{f}}_o, \vec{\mathbf{w}}_o)$  such that

$$\mathsf{NTT}(\hat{\mathbf{v}}_o) = \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \mathsf{RotSum}(\rho_i, \mathsf{NTT}(\theta_i))$$

and

<span id="page-71-0"></span>
$$[y_o, \mathbf{u}_o, \vec{\mathbf{f}}_o, (\mathbf{x}_{w,o} || \vec{\mathbf{w}}_o)] := \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \rho_i \cdot [y_i, \eta_i, \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i, (\mathbf{x}_{w,i} || \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i)]. \tag{48}$$

4. P outputs  $w_o := (\vec{\mathbf{f}}_o, \vec{\mathbf{w}}_o)$ . V outputs  $z_o := (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o, \hat{\mathbf{v}}_o, y_o, \mathbf{u}_o, z_{w,o})$ .

First, we show that V accepts, meaning the verifier check at Step 4 will pass. This follows from the definition of polynomial g (Eq. (38)) and the definitions of  $(\eta_i, \theta_i)_{i=1}^{2k}$ .

It remains to argue that the protocol output  $(\mathbf{x}_o, \mathbf{w}_o)$  satisfies that  $(\mathbf{pp} := (\mathcal{L}, \mathcal{L}_w, \overline{M}), \mathbf{x}_o; \mathbf{w}_o) \in \mathcal{R}_2 := \mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{ccshom}}$  (Eq. (36)). First, by Lemma 3.6, we have that  $(\mathcal{L}, (\mathbf{r}_o, \mathbf{\hat{v}}_o, y_o); \mathbf{f}_o) \in \mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{hom}}$ . Let  $\mathbf{z}_o := (\mathbf{z}_{w,o} || \mathbf{\vec{w}}_o)$ . It remains to prove that (i)  $\mathbf{z}_o = \mathcal{L}_w(\mathbf{f}_o)$  and (ii)  $\mathbf{u}_o = \langle \overline{M} \times \mathsf{tensor}(\mathbf{r}_o), \mathbf{z}_o \rangle$ . Note that (i) holds true because

$$\mathbf{z}_o := (\mathbf{z}_{w,o} || \vec{\mathbf{w}}_o) = \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \rho_i \cdot (\mathbf{z}_{w,i} || \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i) = \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \rho_i \cdot \mathcal{L}_w(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i) = \mathcal{L}_w(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_o).$$

The 1st equality follows from Eq. (48); the 2nd equality holds because  $\mathcal{L}_w(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i) = (\mathbf{z}_{w,i}||\vec{\mathbf{w}}_i)$  for all  $i \in [2k]$ , given the premise that  $(\mathsf{pp}, \mathbf{z}, \mathbf{w}) \in (\mathcal{R}^b_{\mathsf{ccshom}})^{2k}$ ; the last equality holds due to the fact that  $\vec{\mathbf{f}}_o = \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \rho_i \cdot \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i$  and by the homomorphic property of  $\mathcal{L}_w$ .

Similarly, (ii) holds true because

$$\mathbf{u}_o = \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \rho_i \cdot \eta_i = \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \rho_i \cdot \left\langle \overline{M} \times \mathsf{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o), (\mathbf{x}_{w,i} || \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i) \right\rangle = \left\langle \overline{M} \times \mathsf{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o), \mathbf{z}_o \right\rangle \,.$$

The 1st equality is by the definition of  $\mathbf{u}_o$ ; the 2nd equality follows from the definition of  $\eta_i$  in Eq. (47); the last equality holds given the assignment of  $\mathbf{z}_o := (\mathbf{z}_{w,o} || \vec{\mathbf{w}}_o)$  in Eq. (48) and the homomorphic property of inner products.

In sum,  $(pp, \varkappa_o, w_o)$  is in  $\mathcal{R}_2 := \mathcal{R}^B_{\mathsf{ccshom}}$  (Eq. (36)) and the completeness holds. <u>Knowledge soundness:</u> The extractor  $\mathsf{Ext}^{\mathcal{A},\mathsf{P}^*}$  and the running time analysis are almost identical to the proof of Theorem 3.3. The only difference is that the extractor  $\mathsf{Ext}^{\mathcal{A},\mathsf{P}^*}$ , besides outputting  $[\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i]_{i=1}^{2k}$ , also outputs  $[\vec{\mathbf{w}}_i := \mathcal{L}_w(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i)[n_{\mathsf{in}} + 1, n_{\mathsf{in}} + n]]_{i=1}^{2k}$ .

Let  $E_{\text{ext}}$  denote the event defined in the proof of Theorem 3.3, indicating that the extractor recovers two *identical* witnesses  $\operatorname{out}_1, \operatorname{out}_2 \neq \bot$  using two good sets of randomness  $\psi$  and  $\psi'$ . To argue the success probability of extraction, we replace the events  $E_{\text{hom}}$ 

(Eq. (21)) and  $E_{\text{eval}}$  (Eq. (22)) with  $E_{\text{hom}}^*$  and  $E_{\text{eval}}^*$  defined as follows.

$$E_{\mathsf{hom}}^* := E_{\mathsf{ext}} \wedge \left( \forall i \in [2k] : \left( \mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i) = y_i \right) \wedge \left( (\mathbf{x}_{w,i} || \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i) = \mathcal{L}_w(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i) \right) \right), \tag{49}$$

$$E_{\text{eval}}^* := E_{\text{ext}} \wedge \left( \forall i \in [2k] : \left( \text{mle} \left[ \hat{\mathbf{f}}_i \right] (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o') = \theta_i' \right) \wedge \left( \eta_i' = \left\langle \overline{M} \cdot \text{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o'), (\mathbf{x}_{w,i} || \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i) \right\rangle \right) \right). \tag{50}$$

Moreover, we redefine the event  $E_{\mathsf{bad}}$  (Eq. (23)) as  $E_{\mathsf{bad}}^*$  such that  $E_{\mathsf{bad}}^*$  holds if and only  $E_{\mathsf{ext}} = 1$  and there exists  $i \in [2k]$  such that

<span id="page-72-2"></span><span id="page-72-0"></span>
$$\mathbf{u}_i \neq \left\langle \overline{M} \cdot \mathsf{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i), (\mathbf{x}_{w,i} || \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i) \right\rangle \quad \text{or} \quad \mathsf{mle} \left[ \hat{\mathbf{f}}_i \right] (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i) \neq \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i \quad \text{or} \quad p_i(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) \neq 0 \,. \tag{51}$$

To reuse the proof of Theorem 3.3, it suffices to prove the following claims.

<span id="page-72-3"></span>Claim 6. If 
$$E_{\mathsf{ext}}$$
 occurs, then  $E_{\mathsf{hom}}^* \wedge E_{\mathsf{eval}}^*$  occurs. That is, for all  $i \in [2k]$ , we have that (i)  $\mathcal{L}(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i) = y_i$ , (ii)  $\mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o') = \theta_i'$ , (iii)  $(\mathsf{x}_{w,i}||\vec{\mathbf{w}}_i) = \mathcal{L}_w(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i)$ , and (iv)  $\eta_i' = \langle \overline{M} \cdot \mathsf{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o'), (\mathsf{x}_{w,i}||\vec{\mathbf{w}}_i) \rangle$ .

*Proof.* The equations (i), (ii) holds given the proof of Claim 2. To prove (iii), since  $\vec{\mathbf{w}}_i = \mathcal{L}_w(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i)[n_{\mathsf{in}} + 1, n_{\mathsf{in}} + n]$  by definition, it suffices to show that  $\varkappa_{w,i} = \mathcal{L}_w(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i)[1, n_{\mathsf{in}}]$ . Then (iii) follows by replacing  $\mathcal{L}$ ,  $y_i$  with  $\mathcal{L}_w(\cdot)[1, n_{\mathsf{in}}]$ ,  $\varkappa_{w,i}$  everywhere respectively and reusing the argument for (i).

To argue (iv), we observe that the map  $\phi(\cdot) := \langle \overline{M} \cdot \mathsf{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}'_o), (\cdot) \rangle$ , and the map  $\mathcal{L}_w$  are both  $\mathcal{R}_q$ -module homomorphisms; thus, the composition  $\Phi := \phi \circ \mathcal{L}_w$  is also an  $\mathcal{R}_q$ -module homomorphism. Note that if (iii) holds, then (iv) also holds if  $\eta'_i = \Phi(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i)$ , which follows by replacing  $\mathcal{L}$ ,  $y_i$  with  $\Phi$ ,  $\eta'_i$  everywhere respectively and reusing the argument for (i).

<span id="page-72-1"></span>Claim 7. 
$$\Pr[E^*_{\mathsf{eval}} \wedge E^*_{\mathsf{bad}}] \leq \frac{(2b+1)\log m + 6k}{|\mathcal{C}|}$$

*Proof.* The proof is similar to that of Claim 3.7. The difference is that we redefine the polynomial h in Eq. (25) to

$$h([X_i,Y_i,Z_i]_{i=1}^{2k}) := \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \left( \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i - \mathsf{mle}\left[\hat{\mathbf{f}}_i\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i) \right) \cdot X_i + \sum_{i=1}^{2k} p_i(\vec{\beta}') \cdot Y_i + \sum_{i=1}^{2k} \left( \left\langle \overline{M} \cdot \mathsf{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i), \mathbf{z}_i \right\rangle - \mathbf{u}_i \right) \cdot Z_i \,.$$

Note that the sumcheck statement holds if and only if  $h([\alpha_i, \mu_i, \zeta_i]_{i=1}^{2k}) = 0$ . This follows from the fact that for all  $i \in [2k]$ , let  $\mathbf{z}_i := (\mathbf{z}_{w,i} || \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i)$ , we have that

$$\begin{split} \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}} g_{3,i}(\vec{\mathbf{b}}) &= \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}} eq(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i,\vec{\mathbf{b}}) \cdot \left( \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{y}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log(n_{\mathsf{in}}+n)}} \mathsf{mle}\left[\overline{M}\right](\vec{\mathbf{b}},\vec{\mathbf{y}}) \cdot \mathsf{mle}\left[\mathbf{z}_i\right](\vec{\mathbf{y}}) \,. \right) \\ &= \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{y}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log(n_{\mathsf{in}}+n)}} \mathsf{mle}\left[\overline{M}\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i,\vec{\mathbf{y}}) \cdot \mathsf{mle}\left[\mathbf{z}_i\right](\vec{\mathbf{y}}) \\ &= \left\langle \overline{M} \cdot \mathsf{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i), \mathbf{z}_i \right\rangle \,. \end{split}$$

Therefore, we can redefine the events  $E_2$  and  $E_3$  in the proof of Claim 3.7 as

$$\begin{split} E_2 &:= E_{\text{ext}} \wedge \left( h([\alpha_i', \mu_i', \zeta_i']_{i=1}^{2k}) = 0 \right) \wedge \\ & \left( \exists i \in [2k] : \left( \text{mle} \left[ \hat{\mathbf{f}}_i \right] (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i) \neq \hat{\mathbf{v}}_i \right) \vee \left( p_i(\vec{\beta}') \neq 0 \right) \vee \left( \mathbf{u}_i \neq \left\langle \overline{M} \cdot \text{tensor}(\vec{\mathbf{r}}_i), (\mathbf{z}_{w,i} || \vec{\mathbf{w}}_i) \right\rangle \right) \right) \\ E_3 &:= E_{\text{eval}}^* \wedge \left( h([\alpha_i', \mu_i', \zeta_i']_{i=1}^{2k}) \neq 0 \right) \end{split}$$

and the same argument used in the proof of Claim 3.7 can be applied here.

#### <span id="page-73-0"></span>B.4 Proof of Lemma 4.3

Proof. Public reducibility: Given instances  $([\mathbf{z}_i]_{i=1}^k, \mathbf{z}')$ , transcripts that includes  $[\theta_i, \theta_i', \rho_i, \rho_i']_{i=1}^k$ ,  $[\eta^{i,j}, \eta_*^{i,j}]_{i \in [k], j \in [t]}$  and sumcheck challenge  $\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o$ , if the folding verifier accepts, the algorithm outputs the folded instance according to Step 6 of  $\Pi_{\text{batch}}$ , and outputs  $\bot$  otherwise.

<u>Completeness</u>: Given adversarily chosen statements that are in the corresponding relations, we need to argue that the verifier will accept in an honest execution and the folded statement is in the output relation. The argument for latter is identical to that in the proof of Theorem 4.2. The argument for the verification check at Step 4 is also similar, but we need to further show that for all  $j \in [t]$ ,

<span id="page-73-1"></span>
$$\sum_{\ell=1}^{k} b^{\ell-1} \eta_{*}^{\ell,j} = \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{y}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log(n+n_{\mathsf{in}})}} \mathsf{mle}\left[M_{j}\right] (\vec{\mathbf{r}}_{o}, \vec{\mathbf{y}}) \cdot \mathsf{mle}\left[\mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}}\right] (\vec{\mathbf{y}}), \tag{52}$$

where  $\mathbf{z}_{ccs} := (\mathbb{z}_{ccs}, 1, \mathbb{w}_{ccs})$ . This follows from the facts below. First, for all  $i \in [k]$ , let  $\mathbf{f}_i^t$  denote the *i*-th low-norm witness vector in  $\mathbb{z}'$ . For all  $j \in [t]$ , by definition we have that

$$\eta_*^{i,j} = \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{y}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log{(n+n_{\mathrm{in}})}}} \mathsf{mle}\left[M_j\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o,\vec{\mathbf{y}}) \cdot \mathsf{mle}\left[\mathcal{L}_w(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i')\right](\vec{\mathbf{y}}) \,.$$

Moreover, for all  $\vec{\mathbf{y}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log(n+n_{\mathsf{in}})}$ , we have

$$\sum_{\ell=1}^k b^{\ell-1} \mathsf{mle}\left[\mathcal{L}_w(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i')\right](\vec{\mathbf{y}}) = \mathsf{mle}\left[\sum_{\ell=1}^k b^{\ell-1} \mathcal{L}_w(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i')\right](\vec{\mathbf{y}}) = \mathsf{mle}\left[\mathcal{L}_w\left(\sum_{\ell=1}^k b^{\ell-1} \vec{\mathbf{f}}_i'\right)\right](\vec{\mathbf{y}}) = \mathsf{mle}\left[\mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{ccs}}\right](\vec{\mathbf{y}}) \,.$$

Therefore, Eq. (52) holds and completeness follows.

<u>Knowledge soundness:</u> The extractor  $\operatorname{Ext}^{\mathcal{A},\mathsf{P}^*}$  and the running time analysis are identical to the proof of Theorem 4.2. The main difference lies in the analysis of the success probability. Here we need to further argue that the extracted witness for relation  $\mathcal{R}^{b,k}_{\mathsf{splitccs}}$  satisfies the

CCS relation (i.e.,  $(pp_{ccs}, \aleph_{ccs}; \aleph_{ccs}) \in \mathcal{R}_{ccs}$ ). To show this, let  $z_{ccs} := (\aleph_{ccs}, 1, \aleph_{ccs})$ , we define the multilinear polynomial  $q(\vec{\mathbf{x}})$  the same way as we did in the proof of Lemma 4.1,

$$q(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) := \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}} eq(\vec{\mathbf{x}},\vec{\mathbf{b}}) \cdot \left( \sum_{i=1}^{n_s} c_i \cdot \prod_{j \in S_i} \left( \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{y}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log n + n_{\mathrm{in}}}} \mathsf{mle}\left[M_j\right](\vec{\mathbf{b}},\vec{\mathbf{y}}) \cdot \mathsf{mle}\left[\mathbf{z}_{\mathrm{ccs}}\right](\vec{\mathbf{y}}) \right) \right) \; .$$

Recall that  $(pp_{ccs}, \varkappa_{ccs}; \varkappa_{ccs}) \in \mathcal{R}_{ccs}$  if and only if the multilinear polynomial  $q(\vec{\mathbf{x}})$  is a zero polynomial. Similar to the proof of Theorem 4.2, we need to define the bad event  $E_{bad}^*$  and prove that  $E_{bad}^*$  happens with small probability. Here the definition of  $E_{bad}^*$  is almost identical to that in Eq. (51) except that we add that  $E_{bad}^*$  also holds true if  $q(\vec{\mathbf{x}}) \neq 0$ .

Next, similar to Claim 7, we have to provide an upper-bound on the probability that the evaluation check passes while the bad event happens, that is,  $\Pr[E^*_{\text{eval}} \wedge E^*_{\text{bad}}]$ . Here,  $E^*_{\text{eval}}$  is similarly defined as in Eq. (50) except that we add the following predicate: for all  $i \in [k]$ , let  $\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i'$  denote the *i*-th low-norm extracted witness for  $\mathcal{R}_{\text{splitccs}}^{b,k}$ , then for all  $j \in [t]$ , check

$$\eta_*^{i,j} = \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{y}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log{(n+n_{\mathrm{in}})}}} \mathsf{mle}\left[M_j\right](\vec{\mathbf{r}}_o, \vec{\mathbf{y}}) \cdot \mathsf{mle}\left[\mathcal{L}_w(\vec{\mathbf{f}}_i')\right](\vec{\mathbf{y}}) \,.$$

Note that we can obtain an analogous claim as in Claim 6 with exactly the same proof.

Finally, we use the same technique in the proof of Claim 7 to bound the probability  $\Pr[E_{\mathsf{eval}}^* \wedge E_{\mathsf{bad}}^*]$ . A key observation is that  $q(\vec{\beta})$  can be understood as a sumcheck statement, that is,

$$q(\vec{\beta}) = \sum_{\vec{\mathbf{b}} \in \{0,1\}^{\log m}} g'_{\mathsf{ccs}}(\vec{\mathbf{b}})$$

where  $g'_{\text{ccs}}(\vec{\mathbf{x}})$  is defined in Eq. (41). Therefore, by analogously defining the polynomial h and adding the term  $q(\vec{\beta}) \cdot W$  inside h (where W is a formal variable), we can go through exactly the same route as in the proof of Claim 7 to argue that  $\Pr[E^*_{\text{eval}} \wedge E^*_{\text{bad}}]$  is small.
